O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh children, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the result of the gathering of knowledge in the field of medicine, and I have made the end with my explanations and by my declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is twisted and strange in our region and is unknown everywhere, so that science has perished and been forgotten, and there remains only a few small descriptions in books of the ancients who have moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, errors and foolishness have arisen, and the intentions are closed, and the science is abandoned.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will live and thrive by following the order of this treatise according to the path of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and then I will assemble the forms of cauterization tools, and the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of these, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands to be found in our time, the art of medicine has been stretched.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting that he who enters into this subject should master anatomy, as Galen says, so far as he knows the measurement of bones, and their forms and connections and separations, and be acquainted with the bones and nerves and marrow and the number of veins, and the direction of their flow.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this Ypocras says that nails are very foul, and flesh is less so, and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So that anyone who is not familiar with the things said in this book, will avoid falling into error and offending people; thus I have often seen many of those who intervene in this science abandon their knowledge and understanding.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because I saw a madman who cut open an abscess from scrofulous swellings or the neck of a woman, and cut into her arteries in the neck; for this reason so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another madman who tried to break a large stone from an old man's skull; so he carried off a piece of the bladder with it, and was killed inside his own head within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen that it is called for the treatment, and I saw the patient's condition and the size of the wound, and I knew well whether they would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where a certain mire took the treatment of Duke from our land who had broken his leg, and with the breakage he got an infection; and the mires ignorant in handling the break bound the break above the wound with strong ligature, and did not release it from the wound at all, and thus I ended it; and he commanded that he should not be released again; and remained so until his leg was completely infected and his feet and died of perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to release the leg; and when I heard it loose itself, it was peaceful and he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption is already confirmed in the limb, and cannot be cured; and does not cease to corrupt until the member has lost all.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another operation that causes the abscess to burst and infect, and then inflame because of the evil spirit of its rule.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, cannot be cured unless you touch it with iron, if there is not enough time to remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And dearly children, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is to say, whether there is danger in more than one situation; and I will show you in each of these books where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because you must protect yourself, if the physicians do not speak well of you. If you take your arms in comfort, and carefully and firmly take your sick ones, and use the best way so that by God's grace you come to health and are praised; and let fear of illness disappear from sickness; and put away your weapons from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Gauls wrote in some of their admonitions: "Do not take up care for a bad illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and cauterization of aqueous medicine, and they are arranged from head to toe; and the forms of ointments, and metal instruments for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cauterizing wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of ulcers.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and the ordering of the bones just like pieces, and the forms of ulcers.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also as we recall the work, it is necessary to tell the quality of aid and the evil of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and evil are the longest words and subtle science, and the secrets of response; and the more wise men speak about them, and agree with one another; and they reprimand me for my long words, because I am too verbose.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to all kinds of flesh where there is matter; and it helps two kinds of complexions: namely the hot kind with matter, and the dry kind with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry combined flesh with matter, some say that cutting is great help; and others say the opposite: that cutting does not do much good for disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat or cold, and this one who says the opposite that cutting makes great help to hot and dry disease that comes into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you purchase the body of a man and its moisture is in the hot flesh, you find that the flesh is frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this phrase.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have not found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no path should be pursued unless by one who has tried it, and who knows from long experience the cautery of burns, and the variety of human conditions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space for treatment; for us of other kinds we have little hope or fear of maladies cold and moist.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians concur and agree on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery is made from fire so it has the properties of a cure, and is more beneficial than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The fire is simple, and it comes from no other place than the member that is burned, and it does not happen to any other member if its name is mentioned.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The medicines that burn come from member to member by separating, and they bring disease to the afflicted member of healing; and by chance, the fire does not occur in the healthy member because of its high heat and the subtlety of its substance, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through long service and study, which has been revealed to me on the surface of things; and therefore I excuse myself from the length of speech, for it does not please me to reveal the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, as how it cures diseases of the body, just as the philosopher said in demonstrating; now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, how they will agree on when to perform the cauteries, and whom they will choose as assistants.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cutting is beneficial in all times, because the evil consequences are removed by the aid of cutting; and even if the cuts cause painful necessary wounds and hurts, which cannot wait until greater illnesses come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think that a child, for his foolishness; because the disease that is cured by cutting has no return; and they say so; but it's not as they claim, for cutting is not just medicine to heal, but one that changes the complexion, dries out the humors that cause pain, and brings relief sooner than other medicines, through its virtue and power, and by the excellence of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	In cases where disease comes upon him at times according to the complexion of the patient and their nature and virtues; and certain excesses are assembled in him through the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless they administer cauterization on them when they have a small amount of excess and moisture, as cauterization for teeth causes pain, and similar things, then this does not come back again; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the art of medicine, and it's just observation; but they do not believe that cauterization is useful after medicine, their understanding is false, and cauterization is called the art of medicine because when we administer certain types of cures in any disease and they are useless, then we administer the cauterization, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then apply carefully the cautery to the behind of medicine, not according to the foolish opinion of blind men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery made with an instrument of gold is more effective than one made of iron, and they did not say so because of the fire itself but because of the quality of gold and its density; and they said that the cauterized ones do not rot, but I have seen otherwise in some men; and things made of gold are more effective than those made of iron, just as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And it is not known at all when you heat an instrument of gold, whether it will be corrupted by the color of gold and cooling down; and if one heats it too much, they make it in the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have tried on our own work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	or you have ordered this chapter to be written on the head with great pieces, because the vein is lighter to find.
dou cautere olivaire	do cautery olive oil
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is worth moisture and cold on the head, because there's one that we do by the cause of a sickness called "soda", and due to many humors that come down from the head onto the eyes, and ears, and for many pains of the teeth, and pain of the throat, and in itself all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by medicine dissolving the warts, or on the head three times a day, or four times a day, according to what the virtues and the age and the habituation of the patient can tolerate; and then make the wound of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on some cloth; after placing the root of your palm above the root of his nails between his two eyes; and when my hand comes to meet it, if he bleeds from it, take out the cautery which is called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the new signet ink on the wound, and make a small incision and draw out your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand gently, and dress the wound if you see the bone exposed little; if not, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after take some wool, put it in powder and soft cotton inside, and put on the wound, and let it be for three days; after put a moist linen cloth in lard; and let it so that the dressing is exposed; afterwards cure the wound of the ligament which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And when they said the old ones, that as long as it stays on a wound, more blood is spilled; and therefore they take care.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said any of these that one must take such care with the cautery so that part of the bone is burnt, and then reattach what has been burnt by the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say other that you must take such care with the cautery so that it is burnt as far up as possible, and strike it as hard as when you lower a piece of bone to an equal size as one wears for their girdle; because thus the humors come out moved outside; after, you must cure and suture.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two kinds of cauteries do not seem to me to be good in every way, fire whether in some people it gives a view of fear; and I think I must leave them because the bones are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have shown in other members; and even when the joints of the sick person are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more salubrious and soothing for me, then I follow that remedy accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When it is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, and the patient uses herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives of the head, and oils, and ointments; and if one does the cautery which we have previously said, and it is not helpful.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be aware that if the head of the sick person is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cut under that cautery as we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cutting the cautery under each corner of the head until the bone, as we have said before, and perform the cautery as they are called "vasselz"; for this is where one puts vasoconstrictors; and adjust your hand so that you do not see anything until under the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary to make the corne cauteries more subtle than those which are made for the luteinity of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Cut the head with fire
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and the disease is spread to the oil, and the sinews are purged by medicines, and other remedies have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and none of them help: then do cautery according to two manners, namely with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with sharp medicine is this: you take an ounce of alum, and remove the scab and skin around it as well as the two sinews, and then make a small temple to apply the alum in such a way that you can cover the spot again under the skin; and when you have covered it so, bind it well and leave it thus for 12 hours; and then release it and treat with fire again the spot of alum, and let the wound be like two days or three; then put on cotton soaked in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment as long as it is healthy; and if you see, do what I have written about burning medicine or decoctions that I have prescribed to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery to what shape it should be:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the chief is made in the shape of a clover or has little horn, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and put on the painful place, hold your hand tight and turn the heat a little gently, until the edge that hurts is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which lies hidden, and bleed abundantly of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Instruct the patient to put cotton wool on the wound for three days; then put a moist cloth over it; after that apply ointment to the wound until it is healed. And if you want to cauterize this emigration with the "cultellare" tool, which has a point at its tip, and take care not to cover the artery in this emigration which is not old.
de emigraine	of an abscess or boil
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	Since you are treating an abscess as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit from cutting, and observing that what was said about cauterization does not please, then it is fitting to heat the "cultellare" tool until it is white; and so apply a hot oil line on the wound, one half a finger's breadth, and take hold of your hand once; do not strain too tightly, lest you cover the artery, or make it worse as it turns towards the bone; and beware that pain in the jaw occurs when eating, and that there is no numbness but spasms, and let worry for the bleeding of the artery when it is cut be great, just as it was for those who were not skilled and knowledgeable; and leave the wound to heal on its own. But I will tell you how to keep the wound closed when the artery is cut, and show you in this book where it usually occurs.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If the fire cautery does not alleviate the disease, and the patient suffers, cauterize the wound as we have said, and cure the pain until it is healed; and if you see, administer the fire cautery that we have said in the chapter of extraction of the artery, with the fire cautery that has two stitches; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of pain in the ears from cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and there has been no relief from solutives medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not cease, then use this fire cautery which is called "pins", because it takes this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the diseased ear, or on both sides where pain holds, and you are a little apart from the root of the ear after staining it with encaustic; and mark X points around each ear; after the cure, let the ear be so that it is sane.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that must be cured by cautery is not that which burns of fire, but only the one that moves from the swellings, as we have said in divisions of disease; and do not make cautery on similar symptoms that come from the drying and phlegm of the nose.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this similitude of torture that swells from the humors, and from head-sweat, and pharyngitis, and gargarensie, and it is so that you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, and another a little away from the temple, and the third in the meeting of the two lips; and put the cautery in the part where the skin is healthy, and make the point directly to the crown of the ear above a little below the horn of the ear, and another on the temple just as long as an inch; and leave the cautery there until the moisture of the cure is dried.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the likeness of the sawing that we have shown before, but it is slightly more subtle and it is necessary for the cuts to be slightly larger; after treatment let him be as I said, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in the way we have said, but it does not benefit and the sick person has no fever, then do four cauteries: two on each of the two horns of the head, one on the forehead, and one at the "vasselz" (as we have previously said), and a cautery on the lower part of the abdomen, and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of leprosy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease it is necessary to give the patient large and bitter pills for the brain; after dressing, dress the head of the sick person completely, and put a poultice made with sinapis (on the occipital region) on the emplastrure (the application), which is written in the treatment of ointments; and this is the manner of cautery: if you do as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healthy in that way, it's good; and if not, three fire cauteries are made on the swollen head as you go down to the navel, with space between each cautery two of large size; and the cure does as the others do, and if you see a boil, and the patient suffers, make one cautery in the middle; and when skilled is, two other ones above the two horns, and the cure until he's healthy; and let the cauteries be which are called "olivare", as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is fitting that the head be purified with years and what we have said before. After putting on the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and two below the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries above the spine of the back; and let him lie as long as his pain is reduced, and raise your hand; after the cure, until he is healthy, and let be the cauteries which are called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should use fire cautery only on those who are fleshy, and it is advisable to first soften the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffers from many kinds of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it's an infant who cannot suffer, make him gargle and chew bones to soften the brain often with meat; after raising his head a mile high, and then perform fire cautery as we have said before, and do fire cautery on the neck, and each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffers, make it undergo such cauterization as I told one who had paralysis and softening of body, on the spine of the back and neck; and do olive cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, he must do fire cautery subtlety according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are superfluences or corrupted moistures and large pus, then cut with fire cautery as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluences decline to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then give him to drink something by which his brains are purified, according to what is in front in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After he brings the head of the sick person back to its proper place; after cut off a piece of linen well made, like a circle, which you put inside the head; and tie the patient crosswise, and keep him tightly from all parts; after wrap the linen, and pour melted butter of old sheep on it; and let the head heat temperately, so that he can bear to be poured on him; after pour the circle into the head through, and let it cool down; and do this for each sick person once a week with another good government, until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cauterized while doing multiple pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain more; and then wraps cotton soaked in butter and pig fat around it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first due to the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and therefore give to the patient something that is purifying the head, and cleansing all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath several times at dawn.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the command to reapply the poultice, and make cauterize on the inside of the head, and make II cauterize on both temples if there is II weakness in both eyes together, or if one eye has weakness; and strike at all the cautery veins and arteries that are under the wound, and be careful to cauterize long as the temple is wide; and beware of complications of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop the cautery with a great care as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising the art of how to extract them; and at no time have been done cautery or hatereil under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the bowels
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the lumps of the eyelids are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or on the arteries that appear in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it's excesses cold and phlegmatic, then make the cautery as I said at the beginning of the treatment downwards under the eyelids: 1 cautery on the forehead, and 2 cauteries above the two temples, and 2 cauteries under the two bones; and if it needs more, cut with a careful cauterization above the eyebrow.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Body of the eyelid inside the eye
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not bring any relief, then give the patient three bitter drugs; after the king has washed his head, and performs fire cautery on the middle of the cautery olive oil; and perform two cauterizations of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two shoulders, one below the cheeks; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of olive oil is softened by disease and moisture, then apply the cauterization called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	It is because of this
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that cut two cauterics on the same sores just as long as the sores are; and do not let go of your hand unless until the third part of the paper is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	one hair which pierces the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never the case that the hairs of the ointment are converted to paraffin, and pierce the ointment, and then it is done cauterization according to two manners: this means by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and grow even, then put the patient in a healthy place; after that, draw on the paper of the eyes a figure such as the shape of the navel of myrtle, and the beginnings of the sign of the hairs; then put cotton soaked in oil with musk and pepper from persil upon the cut.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have drawn little by little a few times, until the wounds are closed to the end; and the signs of good health of the work are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs raised towards the point of oil; then release your hand, and leave it so for III days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the scab falls off; after apply ointment until he is fully recovered.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow after this; and the paper is softened then again apply cautery to that same place as you did first; if the hairs are fallen off, cauterize it until the paper rises back to its natural place, even and not pricked by the hair.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a piece of parchment in the shape of mint leaf; then take French soap and live charcoal, one of each .2, and grind them together well; and do it hastily if it does not cool down, then place on the eye as if you had made a shape like mint leaf, and put on the paper of eyelids; and if the patient is cured in oil alone, they must be treated with both; and put below the oil a cotton wool soaked in wine; and press the joints of the patient so that your two fingers show above the medicine, and apply .2 to it every time the patient feels biting of the medicine, as he feels it as if of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine is at your debt.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the wound has healed, if you lift the limb so that it is lifted just as it was lifted by constriction of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, put again the medicine on the limb or if the medicine has not worked yet, until your wounds are equal and your eyes are fixed; then put on cotton soaked in butter until the pustules dry up, after applying the ointment called "dyafenis" and other things, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you must guard yourself well on your wound by great care so that the wound does not catch again of the medicine at the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the papers become damp after, and the hair pricks in the oil, then resume the medicine on that person who has been dampened by the paper properly, as you have done before; until the cure is complete; and this is the form of a poultice made with mint.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to those be your constrictions; and do not return to the straight path for him who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not benefit it, then it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a safe place; and bind the menisters' fingers around his head in such a way that it does not move, nor does his head; after binding cotton wet with wine or persillous juice on oil; after cauterizing which is done thus: and if they are bound so as to resemble the shape of a bird's beak, like this it should be done; for if you see, it has been appointed from one side of the head to another; and if you see, it is just like a tent; but all that matters, this which is bound is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula so that it is open, and taking out the pus, and drying it; if it is closed, then apply, and take fire to the bowels; after putting on the cauterizing hot in shape, and holding your hand to the cauterizing at the place not touched by the oil, lest your hands become mad; and put the cauterizing into the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just after the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you repeat the cautery once more, and if it's needed again, and you leave it for three days; after that, put on cotton soaked in fat, and apply a drying ointment to heal the wound, until it is healed, provided that forty days pass and it is healed. Then, put on medicine containing corrosive acid so that the bone may be exposed; and treat according to what he came into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients have mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To treat a fistula, and to cut it open; after that, put in the wound a thin thread so that this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of one .Z. of pus; and hold your hand firmly on the spot, and do not let the patient move at all, until the pus is drawn out and does not run back into the wound; and it is advisable that you put a cloth soaked in wine or oil on the patient's wound: the poultice will serve as a cure for fistula, and will bring about marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have told about, then it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is advisable to administer pus to the wound, and bring the fistula back into the body according to what is most pleasing in its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are fissures on lips called "poil", and even on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures of that which we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not benefit the patient, then apply a small cauterization with a spoon-like knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put him immediately in those fissures until they come into their proper form; after treatment, he shall eat cherries so that he may recover.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or on the uvula or in the mouth or on the roots of the teeth, after it is opened and drained and dried out and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary to apply cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula; after the opening of the fistula, and keeping your hand until the iron hook comes into view again, and on the root of the tooth; and do so once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until he is cured; and if it is treated so, that's good; but if not, then it is necessary to discover the root and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	Any movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and this does not work, then put the patient's head on a warm stone; after put the cautery in the shape that comes next in that manner that you put a cloth over the tooth; and put hot caustic inside the cautery firmly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with vinegar and let them spit it one hour and a half over fire.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the teeth that were moving are fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or if there is coldness in the vein, and medical remedies are not effective, then it must be necessary to cut according to two manners: and cutting with butter and cutting with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cutting with butter if is such that you apply butter from a raven's wing, and the end into a iron spoon or arrow; after putting cotton and wrapping it on the point of a tent, and the pus in butter boils, put on the painful tooth suddenly and hold until it cools down; and so do frequently until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that molten lard and cotton in butter burn, and put on the tooth itching, and put on iron hot until the fire reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the patient to hold a candle made of iron or linen, and let it be so large that the fire does not come close to the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, see how the form will appear afterwards, and place it on the tooth and keep your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be removed on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then wipes away the residue; and it is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on the head that you wish, and according to your power; and this is the shape of the candle:
des scrophules	There are ulcers.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When ulcers are filled with pus and moist coldness, and do not obey digestion through medicines, then apply the cautery to the head so that what follows comes next, and have two apertures for the fumes to come out from the cautery of the other side; and place the cautery on the abscess once, or whenever it seems proper, until the pus of the abscess comes forth. If the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its quantity, and leave it that way for three days; and put moistened cotton wool in butter on top until the ulcer is healed. After care with bandages and poultices until it is safe.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the rope.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures conquer on the channels of the body, and also when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be voided first with soluble medicines; after the cautery at the root of the neck, and beware so you do not come near to the throat again, and do not burn with heat but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the other cautery at the shoulder joint, and the one called "clavicle" because of its shape, we have the form in front of it; and cure the patient as we have said until he is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite. Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of that, the cauterized areas are lighter, because you make three cuts in one.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

After putting the cautery on a perlon (bronze) needle with thread; after he makes the patient rest, and does not keep the limbs in that position for a long time until they are well comforted.

Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When frostbites come to the stomach and there is much moisture that must be extracted from it, and many purgings are given to him, and all manner of accustomed treatments do not benefit him, then it is necessary that the sick person lie on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.

Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment we have had before, until he is cured.

dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy you must perform the following cauterization: take a root of aristolachia as long as you can find, and dry it, and make it just as big and just as long as your two fingers; then cover it with olive oil, and press it to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the lung and the neck, and 2 or 3 times in descending on the part below the beard; and cauterize between the fifth cost and sixth, at an angle after a little; and one cauterization near the breast, and another above the stomach, and between two shoulders, and between two ribs, and do not press with your hand, but rather make it as open as in an odorant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said an old man that no one uses cautery of fire similar to the razor, and the sawing and placing them between the ribs until it comes to that place; and fire takes away the pain, just as we have said in the apostle of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patients die now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of mice

de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire does not value the dropsical, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur. de l’enfleure des piez	of swollen feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in the person who is watery, and filled with a green pus, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and hold your hand tight with the cautery so that you turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply in the center, lest the green pus flow, and apply the cautery as follows:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the second limbs, two cauteries on each leg at the point of the cutlery; and so the cauteries are on the short one in front of the knee and the other behind it in the leg; and let the cauteries be left long to cure, until they come out; after curing the others as we have said.
de la menoison	from the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When stomach problems come from cold and moisture, as long as the digestive virtues are weakened and stagnant in the stomach and intestines, they cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering very much and with great weakness, so do a large cautery on the stomach according to what he has previously spoken about, or cauterize the stomach. Four cauteries on either side of the abdomen subtle, and four cauteries on the hams.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abound and the patient suffering, let them cut fire on the nail, and let fire be applied to each nail, and twice ask for cauterization on the stomach because the cure is helpful when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or one or more of them and are old and are large humors cold, moist, and corrupted, and they have been treated as we have said in divisions, and it has not benefited him, then do cauterization: III apply fire under the spine of the back, that is far from the arm pit, little by little in a triangular manner, and II apply fire under the buttocks; and if you think that its stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and swelling is seen in the face, then apply cauterization to the stomach, as was said before, and II apply to the liver, and II apply to the intestine all over with cauterizing claws, and let the cauterization stay for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let the limb heal until it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelel
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh (thelel), if it seems like a scythe, and then put it completely on fire above the cut flesh, and leave it so long that the cautery comes to the origin of the vein, because it is quick; do this once or twice, and if there's a lot of flesh, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of the instruments, profit from them until they are healthy, and if you cauterize with a great cautery on the cartilage, it will give more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly healed wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear pain or opening, which we will tell about in his own words, if a similar illness comes upon him that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When an abscess comes upon, and is hardened and filled with putrefaction and corrupted moisture, if the doctor probes it gently and notices how far down it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After a cautery burn that resembles a razor, and pour the balm into the abscess according to how much it has entered, and resume the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh are burned away once, twice, or three times, depending on the amount of pus; and beware of burning the nerve which is in question, and great pains.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	For the fistula that is in the body of the testicle and in the intestine, if you take care of this one, do not make it worse by touching it only with your finger, but rather think it is not serious; after the cure, let it be so long as it becomes sane, and if the intestines are inflamed, and the materials are dried for a long time, then know that the intestines are completely healed; and if the materials are not dried, know that the intestines are corrupted, and the bones rot away; and thus as one of these we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.
