When pain from the fruit comes to the kidneys, and of great windiness, and does not come on quickly in a woman, then it is necessary that you do cautery on both sides of the kidneys with the clavicle cautery which we have previously mentioned; and if we are cautering at the midpoint, so three cauteries will be done in line, and if they bring more relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and enfeebled due to fruit and moisture, if the patient holds back urine, then you cut the fire in that part behind the bladder, where the hairs are at the navel, and on both right and left sides, and either one cuts as long as we said with a finger; and you cut backwards over the back, wherever there is need; and whichever one cuts according to the shape previously stated.
de la marris	of the intestines
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the intestines are cold and moist, and do not conceive because of this, and their roots are corrupted and delayed; and when they come out, if it causes great pain: then it is necessary to cut fire into them inside the belly, just as we said for cutting the bladder, and two cuts on the back; and whichever one cuts according to what we said.
de la hainche	Of the cheek
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moistened viscous substance flows onto the cheekbone and because of this movement is hindered from its place, and signs indicate that the thigh is longer than the other when measuring together; and it's found that there are painful movements in the departure of the joint, so it is fitting to cauterize the patient on the cheekbone with a cautery similar to the one used for the stomach; and hold the leaden point inside the circle as it turns, so that the cheekbone is within the circle; and so cauterizes as those who have cauterized the liver.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauteries of olives with large pits, and so cauterize as all the keys; and the doctor until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the groin, and it's from cold and moisture, and patients are cured of what we've said about cutting off division, and a cure does not work, and the disease is old; then it is necessary to purge the patient of thick humors of fetid pills or other hard-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After applying cautery; and the manner of cautery is in two ways: to know, it's about assembling hot medicines, and cautery of fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is in many ways: and one of these is that you cauterize under the groin, three times; to cut off the groin triangle according to this form, and make a deep, strong wound, and space each cautery by the thickness of two fingers, so that the cauteries are olive-sized; sometimes done once on the midpoint above the head of the groin, because it is four in this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the fire cautery is applied to the cautery on a circle as we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the shoulder joint; but make it in such a way that the circle contains all the joint and all the spears are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way one does it in sciatika, when the pain is in the shoulder joint, and cannot be overcome to reach the thigh or the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes to the thigh and knee, he makes two fire cauteries on either side of where the patient says that the pain is; four cauteries above the ankle, one on the left side, a little; whether they are cutting cauteries or burning the thick spears. And if the patient feels that the pain extends to both feet or very close to them, he makes fire cautery on the spot where he feels the pain three times or four at the cautery called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the skill is lost, do more; and if he knows that the pain is located below the knee to the thigh, then do fire cautery on the cauterization cutlery or circular, and take good care in all your cauteries not to do so much cautery as you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not make the patient more annoying and contracting.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who did fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they burnt them so much that the leg became completely twisted, and the feet as well, and it was perceived and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an emetic treatment in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in both upper and lower parts together, do fire cautery on one and the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the learned men of the fire cautery, that this is the manner, to make such a hook and have it as big at the head as one of our sailors with finger breadth, or slightly less, and so inserted between one piece and the other, spacewise according to the length of a penny; and they should be the crosspieces two in number, and also as thick as nails, and there should be one well-made iron hand; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And so heat it until it is entirely red and let it emit the smell of gunpowder, and then place it upon the hook of the sick man's hainche, and turn its surface towards his healthy side; and let it be cauterized once with a cautery, and let him stay three days; after which apply balm to the wound, and let it remain uncovered for a long time; afterwards treat with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sting, and if you see very few who use it; all know that these are the best cauteries, which one can suffer, and where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make a wedge between the two sides, where it falls from the edge of the wound, and be made of iron or linen to a long appearance, and in the high part there should be twice as much, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of two fingers; and over and under, so that they join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the beech leaf on the patient lying on his cost side, and pressing your hand much above the beech leaf; after gifting between the two circles of the hot water which is heated a little in the fire, let him stay one hour, taking away the heat and the burning from him.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the molar extraction, instruct as you do for fire cautery; and when molar extraction fails, take hold with the instrument and lift the cheek with a soft hand, and let it be so for three days, and put butter until the decay in the extraction site is gone; and let it be three days that purtification takes place; and that would be the rear aid after the cure of wounds, until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread just to the thigh or just to the leg, make an instrument like the one you have made in the cheek more so; and that is the way of applying warmth, and I wrote it in treating of medical correction.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and gypsum, equal amounts of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If the small opening does not prevent the point of a razor from entering; and place another pot well filled with fat, and put above chili and chalk and powder soft as much as you have two above the powders when you will have taken it to your hand; and leave thus until it comes out hot and bloody or full of fat, then take all that and put on chalk and on chili so.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And if it is very hot and becomes moist due to the moisture of various medicinal works and cauteries of other members, for it makes all these works like fire, and other medicines that we cauterize well, so as to cut the vein just so with thread and honey acacia and chalk with soap, all these sweet things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galen tells us of a cure for one man who was cured of vein pain and sciatica, and how great he praised it, saying that no other cure was necessary, and that he became whole after one time when this cure was done, and he had bathed as he teaches here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	Instruct the patient to hold a green and fresh liver in his left hand, and crush it with a little fat, and place it on the haunch, on the thigh or where the pain is felt, and bind him; and let him stay for three hours, by the quantity that the patient feels no more irritation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him into the water or bath until his body is a little flushed out, and put him back into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that none of these medications should be used on the body after evacuation.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatica vein is cauterized with sheep's intestines, if it helps much; and he must be made to do this in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and anoint it with old oil, and put it on the hollow that is between the little toe and the other which is called the flesse.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried cheese, and putting it on fire until it is like charcoal, put it on linen, and let it stay until it becomes soot-like; repeat this again, and do not stop doing this until you think by touch that it has reached the point where the pain will cease; for this kind of cautery is called "cautery of cheese".
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes on, whether by falling or from impact or due to excessive blood evacuation, or when it seems that there is an expansion of cold material, none of these symptoms value cautery, except for those who come from the infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be free of fetid pills or other similar things on his back, where the pain lies, three lines marked out in length, and for each line V cauterys are performed or more according to the virtue and quantity the patient can bear; and it should be done the cautery as is called "poins"; and if you see this, do III cauteries or IV at the cautery of the clavicle half-mooned according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes upon small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow ribs when they straighten up, and fear; and you will find in the back spine on their back and at this appearance which comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you view him being cured, if you cauterize at the cautery of a cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery stains each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that cutting into the spine causes two or three lines of marks, and the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment, let him remain as long as he is sane according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply fire cautery in a groin area where there is inflammation of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by swelling in each limb of the body, and when the pain comes from the foot, they call it "podagre" properly, and when it is due to cold causes and medicines cannot cure it, then it should be cured with fire cautery in this manner: make a hole with fire cauteries around the joint of the foot, and apply olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	If it has need to prick at the face of the foot, then let them perform cautery on all the cautery as they claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then let them perform cautery on each knee three cauterizations or four on each part, on all the olive oil cautery; and if you have need of more, do more, but don’t hold your hand too far over the fire until it is blackened.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knees and on the back, then let them administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then let them insert pins into the flesh two lines; and if there is no pain remaining, you must let it heal on its own, but if it does not go away, let's do pinches on each joint and on the skin of the hand; and if pains come to the elbows or shoulders, let's cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and use medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If you do good governance and purge the humors, then you will be healthy again by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the cut of the sinew.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a cut comes to the flesh and the bowels descend to the joints and it is new, then it is advisable that when you cure the wounds, do not make the same thing the next day; and use things that cleanse the belly, so that the fumes descend from its belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to twist his ankle until the flesh is healed, and tie it with your hands, and mark the sign of a half-circle above the bone of the finger, and in such a way that it be like a circle above the body; then take off the cautery which has this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	So long as he is white and has sentels.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then tie up the bowels to their place; and let the ministers keep his hand away from returning there; and work well on the patient, and put a cloth and a servant over the thighs, and another under the leg which keeps his hands; then put the cautery on the sign at the tip of your finger, and your right hand and your thumb until you touch the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, so that it comes out again another time until you grow old enough to touch it; and watch carefully that the bowels do not sail when you make the cautery; do not burn them; and thus let the patients not die, or from some other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you will know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct the cauterization of children to be subtle according to their measure, and of great men also in proportion to theirs; after three days cure them with butter cautery until the scab is shed; after treatment for other ointments until they are healed, and care for the patient for forty days on his back so that the wound is well covered; and it is necessary that their nourishment be prolonged long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he goes to bed in chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, give him a well-made bandage, and pour on him forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against excessive consumption of wine and eating, and excessive breathing. And when you follow this teaching, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after cutting on his shoulder blade.
de la routure dou ventre	of the surgery of the abdomen.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When such wounds come to other abdomens and become known, and you see that they do not grow again, cut the wound according to its size, and burn off one third of the fever; after the treatment, as we have said; and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized at three angles like this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark first the left of the incision and make a line for the width of the wound, and another further away, and take out all the cauterization nails.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and more bitter.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, or from a fall or from an injury, and the pain persists for a long time, and no cure of medicine is effective, then it is fitting to cauterize with the cautery called "poins", and to do the cauterizations according to the length, thickness, and weakness and virtue and location of twisting and of pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If there is strength in the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat the other cautery on that one, because it is customary to make the member move as it is nearest, so that you may do cauterizations until the patient becomes whole.
de meselerie	Of skillfulness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The problem is not cured with cauterization alone by great means, and the disease itself that comes from rotting flesh and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You cannot see the cauterizer being effective, be on guard if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, do not pierce or let it remain, for you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the whole patient, then perform cauterization on the head: I cover the head with wool, and the other towards the front of the eyebrows; two above the ears, and one behind the ear; and keep your hand away until the cauterizing comes to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the big humors can escape; and cauterize on the mice according to what is in front of it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the mesentery is everywhere sparse; and it manifests itself, so it is fitting that you cauterize with these cauteries which we have said about in the head, and one cauterizes on the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and one on the cupola, and another under the scapula, and two under each shoulder, and two on the buttocks, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the cavities of the hands; and beware not to burn those that are under the skin calcified, lest you do so; and at no time cauterize on the bone of the finger, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that as you do more cauterizing, the more it will help, and the more it will benefit; and know that patients feel no pain at cauterization if they are healed, because their body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that cauterization should be done both large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in various types of instruments.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment let him eat white flour mixed with honey and other remedies until he is cured.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an edema comes upon any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then you must perform cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and put one cautery in through the flesh of the wound; then treat the limb with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is made by hand and foot and back at the end of the nerve that mutes the member, and thus if it causes swelling; and whoever tries to intervene without knowing the members and their movement of the body will be wrong.
de albaras	of bars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called “bars” is old and the art of medicine has no value, then cut it with a cautery a little in depth, according to the quantity of the flesh that is cut, until the wound is stopped and its color; then feed the patient flour made with whey and lentils with olive oil and leaves of plantain, and blood from chickens and goose blood, each one a part; and mix all together, and tie it in a bandage, and apply to him as long as he is well.
li cure de chancre par cautere	Treatment of the chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the chancre comes at the beginning, and you stop seeing it, cut it with a cautery that seems like a circle all around its circumference.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Instruct all wise men that cautery should also be performed at the center of an ulcer; and I do not think this is good, for I fear it will cause ulcers and corruption, and I have never seen such a thing happen; and there is no surer way than to cauterize around, with the "circle" cautery, as we have said in many other cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of an edema that cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it does not die or because of the fluidity it makes or because of the age of the sick person when they are old and have little blood or time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries, after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced with the fire cautery, so that it takes shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the fire cautery pierces the liver, so that the cautery takes on the appearance:
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is completely cured.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease which is called "corrodens", and is nothing other than an ulcer on a limb, because it infects the limbs just as the fire eats away at dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in someone who can suffer fire cautery together, then take the fire cauteries small and great, according to what is needed for the patient or where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until you have removed all the corruption, and there remains nothing of it, that everything which is corrupted should be destroyed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him lie three days, and place the patient on fire cautery to suffer burns with oil until the scalded skin is destroyed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of flesh born from wounds.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that no healthy flesh is born, it's good; and if not, repeatedly cauterize those who have remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy is sometimes treated with medicated water instead of fire cautery; but every time fire cautery is used it is a greater help, and I have said before the remedy for medicated water in the division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pears that come to the joints
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, at the joints due to wear and tear, a disease comes into being which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a big thing that causes pain.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cauteries for this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	Which is to say cauter with fire and cauter with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautering with fire is that you should heat the cauter like a heated needle as well as a pen of vulcanite, and it should be made from good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail in all parts, and have subtle margins. After that put the whole hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail so long as it comes out with a burnt spot; then leave it like this for three days until it starts to rot; then make an emplastrum of fresh mulberries crushed with resin, and let the emplastrum on the entire night, and the nail will come loose and be descaled from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to treat the joint with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted by foul odour of the body, and has often happened in hands and feet, so that you must apply fire cautery to warm water; and thus: take a cane of iron or linen, or a quill of vinegar, and put on the nail and the nail bed, as one presses warts; and put the cane on it so that it pricks all around, then put some warm water in and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and you can find the warm water deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer a little the burning of the warm water for an hour; and then let it be, and all will come out at their roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So that you may do after another, until you have examined all those who are in the body, then treat the joints which obstruct movement.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shiver from cold or fever, or a quarter-fever, or any other, it is fitting that you make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the skin, and one on the stomach at the olive cauterization; then let them stop shivering, and hasten their recovery from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of pustules that are putrid.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear by accident on the body bathes, or putrid pustules, which come from great corrupted masses.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary when they first appear that we do a cautery on each of the head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of a fustel made from myrtle wood, so that the point may be gripped by the fire, or with an aristolochia root long, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time should the cautery be done at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and it will not cause them to grow in size ahead, but breaks off the superfluous flesh that comes from there, and cures; but it is necessary to do so after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the arteries are cut open.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great bleeding from the artery that is cut on the wound, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and such similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to hasten whenever this happens to anyone, so you apply your index finger on the wound of the vein and strain it very much until the pain is appeased below your index; then put the olive oil cautery in small and large quantities as they are all red; then grasp, either great or little according to the wound and how the artery is routed, and place the cautery above the vein where you hold your index, and keep it there until the pain does not remain.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the fire jumps up when you lift your index finger above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hold of another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until they are all extinguished; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is near, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when there is no discharge of the artery, it cannot be well restored by itself because the artery is large, unless it happens by one of the four ways we have mentioned: or through cautery, or through extraction since it has not been treated, or with strong binding of thread, or with medicines applied which have power to stop the bleeding; and let it happen as a consequence.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will stretch back the joints tightly wrapped in cloth or place hot things upon them, or other similar things, if it does not profit him at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has not taken any medicine or remedy, then he must place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well so that it remains stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not stir him, but let him feel cold water frequently until he is frozen stiff, so cold that when he has stopped bleeding, he becomes swollen and solid and remains stretched.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter, when it is necessary to cut with fire or hot medicine, and what can be treated with cautery, and the causes and symptoms and forms of treatment; and I wrote that chapter on the head just as if it had been written by pie. And I will go through this same path because that's how one finds the quickest solution for what is sought.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there are more danger and fear than with the first cauterization, and for this reason it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to venture into madness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come in for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they die easily because of the severity of their disease and the great power of their evil; and for these reasons one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these ones who come to me with their condition, and says: "wait, I am cured"; and the sickness is pitiless.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you should only be willing to treat those who come to you with this condition, but put more great consideration in your honor than in your own wealth; and do not be feeble-mindedly but rather wisely of those things from which you are certain, and for which you have taken possession; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your sick patients so that a cure is converted to salvation; and this will help you to attain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear children, Our Lord grants you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you in the order of chapters, according to what is before or after a cautery chapter, which I have devised for you from the head down to the feet, because you will find it more easily that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Fill your head with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	It is known that this illness comes often in children at birth, and when the child holds his head too tightly; and sometimes it occurs from a reason returned which one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness in adults, and all those that I have seen have had a severe death; and therefore it seems to me that one should exercise caution with these treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	In this affliction the child has swollen flesh, and the head swells every day until it cannot be sustained; and so strong is the moisture that he is believed to have died, and this moisture so forms beneath the bone above the spleen, between the heart and the bone; and such wounds are caused by the moisture being between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you must cut open with a broad fissure in the head, as long as two of us, until the swelling ceases; and observe this form of spatulate
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deeply seated, and the abscesses are larger, cut two incisions in the shape of a cross.
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the commissures of the head are swollen on each side, and the fluid bursts forth when you press with your hand into it, but does not return: then it is necessary to cut three incisions in the head according to this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After tightening the torn sheets and powders, and putting in wine and oil, and leaving it so for a fifth day; then remove it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head drain completely, and give the patient dried meat of a little moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look at or open the size of the abscess, and the assembled water; for sometimes it is before, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then at or when the abscess is opened, and the filling of the water, and cut according to what you have the skill; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and apply a sufficient amount of blood, so that the patient dies from the consequence of bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the loin
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to anyone who is called a "catering" or the worst, and the disease is ancient, and medical remedies do not help, then the last resort is to apply cauterization with what we cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary that you cover the eyes when they are done reappearing on his head; after he rubs it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull out the disease from his neck all with one strip of cloth; then examine if there is blood on either side, and near the ears, and not long to recover; then mark the sides of the veins afterwards, then cut one and the other with a good spatula, two parts thick, until it reaches just to the bone, so that they be as wide as the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	If you see, pour out the spatumile below the artery and cut on top, as you should when going through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And if the vein is cut, so it bleeds continually without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not open to feel, it is best that you measure the quantity of space three times (dozens), then sign and make it as tight as possible; and put a poultice of fire on it six or seven times, in case there are one more or less than that, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if there is still an exposed point on the bone, do not open the incision further because it may cause bleeding again, then extract the wound and bind, and provide treatment with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	le fire cautere
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old blood comes out, and a cough is good, because of the moistness of tears and the heat in the temples and the ancient sore spot and similar things, and it is treated with various kinds of medicine cures, but none of them benefit him, so we have to extract the arteries from the temples and the cauterized areas, as we have previously mentioned.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the sick person makes his hair behind their temples, and listens to where the artery opens in the temple, because it opens well by its pulsing, and is not much swollen like in some people who are too cold; and if it is swollen, he strains off the skin of the patient with certain draperies, then flogs him with a rough cloth, and raises him from a hot water as long as the artery becomes clearly visible; then takes the spatula which has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scorch the skin lightly until you see the artery, then take it upwards with pinches, and pull well from the skin that is below each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it by the point of the needle, then cut according to the quantity of two bones.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, do not make a movement without pain in all parts.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take blood from the sixth [finger], just two and a half; and if the artery is large, it is fitting that you tie it with two levers of a double-strong thread of silk, so that no pus will appear before the swelling of the wound, and come back repeatedly with blood; then cut the overflow that is between the two levers in the same hour, and then, if you see, since he has been cauterized with cautery cutellaire just up to the bone until the bones are cut, this is the gentle work, if the patient does not have fever and it is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery, it is aid to finish the moistors: because of this, it is more help for moistors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, he fills it with his own vein of wool and puts on well-made tights; and when they are pulled out, if some medicine is applied that causes inflammation, and tentatively so until it heals; and if you do not have a cut from the artery after you work, then hasten to cover it by fire cautery, or take out the vein with your hand, lest it be unseated; and if you don't have that, put wool on the vein as thick as it can hold, and apply cold water until it stops flowing, and is strained as necessary; for what is pulled too soon and more easily in extracting an artery is to cauterize a vein of this cautery with two parts, but they should be well-spaced to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too dark, he holds less his heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And he must have two sharp knives, one of great force, and then when you have a bandage on the two areas, hold the hot iron above them until it comes to the bone, cut the vein in two areas; and let be separated between the two joints because there is no soldering of this cautery throughout; and this is the form of cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing into the veins that are on top of the forehead, and he does not benefit from any medical treatment that we do, and you see the face of the sick person reddening, and feel his front feeling as if he is lame; and the oil is cool and moist so that the hair of the scalp is wet, and the scalp is scorched by the heat of the tears, if it requires this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to be called 'cure contused', and make him cut his hair again, so that he has either a front or two fowls in front, equally according to the length of the front; and let one of them be as if two doves were broken on the front, advancing forward and downward just like a newf; and let the others be like two birds above the papers, and guard yourself from cutting the arteries which are at those places above the papers; and hold back your hand from continuing the two mandibles, and make each wound the quantity of three doves across; and bring an apple sponge with a lot of rags to absorb the blood, then bathe it in a good spatumile with two parts of its shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut at the temple just above the second incision; scorch all the bleeding that is between the two wounds until you reach the syphac which is on the bone, then make another part from the main incision just above the other second, and then pull out that spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick in the first cut with the instrument called "culterial", and it is very sharp from one side and soft from the other, not sharp at all, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the knife cutting towards the raw flesh at the wound, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off all the vessels that flow from the head through the eyes until the incision is continuous, just as far as the opening of the wound; then make another cut in the middle, just up to the other edge; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the liquid from the wound; then put a linen strip over each cut, and place over it damp cloths soaked in wine and oil and spices, and keep away from spreading abscesses; on the third day, untie the bandage, and administer great quantities of watered-down plantain juice, then apply the Basilicon salve with olive oil, and other remedies for wounds, until he is cured.
dou reume des eulz	Do something to the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any vein becomes swollen due to custom, and you see the eyes cloudy and small, and weak the sight, and the eyelids burn; and the skin is pulled back, and the pain is in the forehead, and the patient sneezes; then know from these accidents that those materials and that catarrh come only from many veins, and what this medicine is for, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to touch their forehead, then make a great cut in the middle of the forehead, and another small one.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and make an incision just until the bone; and keep your hand away from the skin of the temples that move more at the pain; and when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision and put cotton wool and linen threads there; then tie wet cloth strips in wine and oil, and be careful not to puncture the abscess; when it is cauterized, it is necessary that you rub the bone until it starts to come out, then treat with excising things which make it heal.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of powdered coal, and mix them together; and administer to these wounds for fear of fire throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear-bleeding
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of four things: grains, or beast, or stone from the mine, or similar thing like metal; or seed, like poppy, fennel, and weeds; or fluid, like water and ash, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes out of the ear stone or another kind of thing that does not attach itself to the ear, nor grows in the ear, if you put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill some small amount of violet oil or silex oil, and administer extraction. Then make it vomit condisions, and stop the nose when vomiting comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and make the ear lie above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	A lot of times comes force by this treatment; and if it does not come quickly, then they must apply extractions with subtle fingers, because there is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it falls by the fingers, that is good; if not, then apply extractions with a small pinching at the root; and if it does not fall by that, make an application of resin and pour the head into the canna or ear passage very strongly, so that what is near the canna can be blocked with wax so that no needle can enter with the canna; then break off the force, because often comes to be like we said; and if it does not come to be in this manner, take glue of which you catch the birds, and put some on some instrument which has a point for this purpose, and put cotton inside; then press the glue onto any stone or thing, and break off the force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all those things that we have said, so hasten to pierce the ear thus before incising the abscess and spasm; and the manner of piercing is such that you first make the patient healthy of the head, and extract the blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small piercing in the root of the ear at the fat or where it depends; and let the piercing be as a moon, until you come to the bone, then break it according to your power, and suck it hasteningly into your mouth; and the cure shall be complete when they are healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that has settled and it swells, extract the infection; and if it cannot come out, then administer a small spot of poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not cut it when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, so many times that you have cut away pieces; then take out small pinches and at the root, as we have said, so that the extraction may be smooth.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then it is appropriate that the patient coughs into the ear; and fill the ear with woolen cloth.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be placed above the same ear or in water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If that happens because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.
