If it does not happen because of this, then pierce many pieces according to the length that you must hold and light ones, and let them sit over the fire; and put a piece of bone in the ear, and set foot on the other part, and feel from one bone on top of another bone on the ear; and do not cease to make this movement of bone on bone until the water is all gone, and so will it be all gone; and if you see, pierce the joint, and push one of the bones into the ear, and the other foot gets set over fire until the joint is ardent; then redo another part of joints as long as the water is all gone, just as we have said in the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the vein, if it is small like an insect and similar things, cure as we have said in division; but if it is large so that you can feel it, take out the pinchers extraction; and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms, take out the ears as we have said in division and when treating swellings; if the cure does not profit, it is necessary to look at the ear towards the sun: if no worms are seen, use subtle pins, and if they are not found, take the chain, for this is the shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it can be narrow under and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle pin in the ear according to the quantity of pain in the patient, then follow it to the root. Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, so they are stopped within the cotton tube as I said in the vein; and if they do not burst like we have said, administer enemas as the ancients have proven in the operation of worms, and you will find or treat for enemas; and if you pour your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, so that it is in the form that you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or lead poured into the small openings, and over them for distillation; and to press within the distillation with the well-made instrument of lead, and if you see the razor and enveloped in the point of the cotton, then pour your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the tube, so that the tube is in the ear; then put the razor into everything the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or almost coming out of the ear; and it feels to the patient inside, and if the distillations are heated a little as when we distill in the ear; and guard that they do not get too cold, for the medicine would be bad.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the bursting of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some defect in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults by bursting of a wound, or by chipping something inside the ear, and this bursting comes sometimes through the bottom of the ear if you can't see it; and sometimes there is no defect at all, but they see very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This one that comes through from the inside if you can't see it is due to an internal disorder in many cases, and in this case, it's necessary to put the ear of the sick person in sunlight; and look inside: if you see any opilation (whiteness), then the cause has a form like this
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And whether it is pus and swelling in front and behind all of the pain, if you do not bleed the ear; or if the opilation comes from a bone or part of the ear, if you have subtle pinpricks and carefully strike it lightly, until that bone is entirely broken.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the prickles are in the ear, take a fine snarer and apply it to the inner part of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the prickling in the ear, which patients feel as great pain in the ear, cut slightly and keep from over-treating the ears; then put into the ear a tent of some size according to the width of the perforation, and apply Egypt's ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do this on any day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and apply its ointment in rosewater, and powder over it with vitriol powdered; and if you see that the ear has swollen, cover it so that you treat the tent and move another wet tent made of olive oil and beeswax, until the swelling subsides; then cure as long as it is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood accumulates in the ear, plunge an sponge into it and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments to remove the accumulation of blood that are used for treating discharges.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Cover the eyes with a mixture of moist and dry paper when they are wet, so that you should stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut off one root with a spatula; then put on vitriol solution.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without cutting off, the cautery is done with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cautery is applied after the incision is made, and it takes several times to repair it, so that none of its roots remain; and when they are cauterized by fire, their roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	From the flea
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come in paper some things that resemble lice in form and hardness, and because of this, is this disease called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the symptoms are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side and another, and it's an easy thing to know; do therefore the large cuts, then scorch each part lightly, then take them with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it with a small cut in the paper, so that nothing hurts the patient; and if the fissure is large, if the assembly has a seam, and treat as long as it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply any force, for the ointments restore it at once and irritate the skin.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et se li grandine is falling down into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper, and hold the dust in one pinches, and press it from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it brings no harm; and when the dust is pressed, take off the salty water oil and cure the patient as long as they are sick.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyelids
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	In that fat is a grease that gets tangled in threads of paper above, and it happens to children with no one to care for them, and causes great pain to their eyes, and they come to have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look towards the light of the sun because the tears run into their eyes; and for this reason they lie on their faces afterwards, and sleep on, and are their paper above their eyebrows moistened that the inflow and appearance change from the exinach which opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lever to your right hand and feel it sticking inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of its work is that the patient puts his head in your hands; and then take a linen strip, and tie a tourniquet around it according to the quantity of the sticking inside each part, then put it on; press with one hand from the other side until the sticking becomes assembled inside the circle; then cut at the midpoint of the swelling near the spur of cutting an artery of a vein; and be no greater than the wound you made in the vein; and make the leather in proportion as long as you reach to the sticking; and in various positions, the sticking comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Instruct the patient to tie with one piece of cloth gauze between the two bones without fail, and turn his hand in both right and left until it is spread out; and guard that you do not add anything to the wound, lest you become like a full-grown gnat stuck in oil.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open in the beginning of the wound, tie with a little cloth around it lightly until it appears; then cut as we have said, then moisten with soft cloth and water, and bind it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if some such men who are breaking ropes and laying on it to corrupt that remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer so long as he remains sound.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the joint of the arm hot, so that the healer gives it emplastries soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hair from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper are born, and are wilted, such that they hurt the eyes, and cause various maladies, as accustomed tears and swellings of the papers, so that it is a cause of destruction to the eyes; and it's a cure in four ways: either by cautery with fire together, or by aqua according to what is before or in the chapter of cautery, and done either by incision and stitching, or by bandages, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the sick person on your healthy one; then turn the paper with oil in your left hand; if it's turned, it's good; if not, take an awl and cut through the thread above it. Either cut along the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing from the edges of these hairs, cut the thread upwards on both sides of the paper, and turn it with a razor; then make in the underside of the paper, beneath the hairs that adhere, up to the length of the small margin, cutting all along the seam from the big to the small. Then pull out the thread, and place under the paper a small tent made of linen and fabric, then sew on the paper an image of an enche, as with the mite of myrtle, and whatever you see take in proportion the quantity that is written on all papers so devised.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Instruct the patient to apply a certain quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then make it all over the skin on the two lines you have signed, and start with a large needle just after a small one; and sew one of the incisions close to the natural hairs in the size of a finger, then pour something in one of the two corners, then scrape it whole; then assemble the two lips to a sewing with an anchor-shaped needle with all the fine thread of linen, and wipe out the blood, and make the skin dry on the two eyebrows at any sticky thing; if you have seen this done, then do so; and if not, just leave the stitching and the threads just after three days or four; then treat the wound with a drying and tightening thing, because the paper lives in the moment of the wound and the assembly of it, but the sewing is worn (as the ancients said), and this is work done with fear; and if you have another method: and thus sews the skin according to the figure that is similar to the fuel of myrtle, as we have told, three inches away from each other according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off that which overhangs equally, according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are not able to hold the tongs, and what is cut off is not even, then prick an awl or it has a thread, and sew into its shape; and sew the other thread around the big seam, and the small one around the little, and assemble them evenly between your two fingers; then secure your hand evenly, and secure all the skin above where you have stitched, as we have said before, and sew the two lips of the wound by stitching, until it is healed. And if an abscess comes to your incision, then cauterize it with cerote and similar ointment soothing; but at times happens that the hair of the papilla are converted: so it is fitting that you use what we have said about cutting; but the suturing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the knees is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the flesh inside according to what I have said, and then make two hinges by art, and two subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the widened space of the spatula are; and cut at two hinge bones where you hold the strings; then assemble one and the other subtly above what surmounts from the oil paper, and strain the two hinges from the two parts formed; and let it be in this way for some days, and the ligament that is tightened will die and turn and heal, as much as it will feel by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late and the cut has some force, then treat it until it is sane; and when the wound is sewn, and if there is raised paper, and no longer will the hairs grow; and this is the form of the two hinges that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Instruct the head of the chase to be treated so that the hairs do not come forth with it, if you treat the head of the chase thus, then treat it below at all the filaments that you have ordered, until the chase comes forth from the perturbations above and you see it by means of the vision of oil; then treat the chase and the filaments, and close the oil and let the other one close II days or III, so that the hairs grow in their place and bring forth a char on top; and if small hairs are present, accompany I long hair from the cheekbones, nature is drawn towards them, and lift it with that one which you leave, until they become elongated and then let it be.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's corruption
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	How this illness, which is called "aleacratis" or corruption of the oil, comes to be, there are two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or incision, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treating this wound is that you cut through the sutures, and dress the lips, and put in linen tents, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not advisable to use in the treatment of wounds those things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than it was at first; but working with softening things, like fenugreek; and the rose of water or oil, or seed of flax are cooked, and ointments made from diyaquilon melted in any of the oils, and a tent is wrapped around, and thus the cure.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	The treasures of your cure are that you guard yourself so they do not change shape according to the original form; and this work we have said does not bring harm but only in a similar manner to this disease, which it returns according to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the charcoal that comes into the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is outside what truly is called "axacrati", and is natural in origin.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things; and the view of the work in it is such that you pierce with an arrow, because it has two filaments, and the point in the charcoal, and make it pierce from the left side to the right shoulder so that the filaments come out in two joints of the charcoal; then put the charcoal on top over all the arrow, and strike with one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or sewing or cautery, so it is fitting that you cut a plain incision below the hairs of the papers; and according to what was said before; then sew between the two fingers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters take great care that by some power or skill he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick ones themselves, according to what they need treatment and incisions of many kinds.
dou soudement de la papiere	When a piece of paper suddenly cuts
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	So that the cut piece of paper can be smoothed out with the white of oil and will not move or do its natural work, if it so happens then you must put a razor point on the paper, and lift it up; and make a stitch as carefully, as you copy what is fine at the stylus penile subtle, which should not be too harsh nor too sharp, so that the sick person cannot suffer from the stylus being too harsh or staining the oil; and let your incision, where you scrape off that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape; and it is healed whole that assembly, and it happens never again in the oily sauce, and washes with a gentle water and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil larded mutton fat in abundance of udder; and after three days use the vinegar and such swift things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the oil of the hog
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of hog fat: one is nervous and resembles dried, thick skin, and another that isn't nervous but looks like pale, frozen moisture, when touched with iron it causes pain; while both have a similar appearance near the great vein, they gradually fill up and cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of cutting is that the patient puts their head on a clean cloth, then opens the eyes; lifts the paper to their hand, then cuts the hog fat into small double folds and makes a stab above; takes an needle and fills it with horse hair, or wool, or bull skin, and makes a strong thread; doubles the point of the needle slightly and stabs the hog fat, piercing all the way through the needle, ties the hog fat to a thread and makes a stab above, then scrapes off all the hairs on the cost of the hog fat which lead to the spot where the blood vessel opens up to the skin, just at the top of the head, then chops off the remaining part at the root of the vein until it reaches the fine and subtle veins; leaving the natural color or the vein alone, if there is no bleeding from the vein as used to be. And sometimes the hog fat is only tied on, and to the thread, as we have said; then scrapes off all the skin so soft that this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the physician to take care that the scab not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the purpleness is not perceived; and after the incision, grieve in oil a little bit of chopped silk, and on the neck make it sit for until the next day; then the physician should deal with what is required so that he may be healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the ingrown nail is not numb and you cannot push the needle in, and the nail can't enter, this condition is often cured with medicines; and as I have explained in the division, and if you see a covering on it, apply oil to the patient, and take the scab lightly and good according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And if you take out the ingrown nail subtlety, and if you see that it does not decrease at all and the reason is pressing it, then distill from your mouth into the oil made with litarge and red vinegar, and put in oil on the neck; apply the oil until the next day; then resume work as of this same operation, until it is completely hollowed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no trouble is found in the eye, like a boil on the eyelid, then apply cold and cure the boil so that it heals, then resume the work as before until it heals.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin around the eyelid is swollen at night due to great disturbance, and you press it with an onion slice, and only cut a little part, so that no blood comes out; then distill in the eye coriander juice red which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the eyelid.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	If some men do not get any red flesh, and cover the eyelid and restrain it on bandages and torn parts away from it, and it seems like a rose of balsam; then if the wound is made such that the patient puts his head on a safe one, then open the eyes, and cut all that flesh with convenient lines as we have shown in the incision of the ulcer and with small forces so that the form appears after this chapter as it demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, apply the oil of silymarin or distill coriander juice red and similar medicines corrosives, and put on the eye cotton with vinegar, so that it be certain of an ulcerous boil; and if it does not remain anything, and the patient gets up without being able to walk, and you doubt about an ulcerous boil, then leave the oil and cure the ulcer with soothing medicines for ulcers; then return to your work until it heals, and do so when all the wounds are cleaned in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you adjust the treatment for each type of weakness of the body through natural means, and through accidental means, in the presence of iron; and do not put your hand on any of these operations until you see if this member will suffer from that operation.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	But these eyes are red ones that cover the skin, and they take away their sight and weaken them every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore to be done first that you look at the skin, in what manner it is, because if it is inflamed, and there is no other disease of fire than the inflammation; then the treatment is thus: instruct the patient to place his head on a healthy one, then suspend those eyes for as long as possible according to his wisdom, and let the subtle eyelids double in that form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two points by degree in the joint according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil around the veins with gentle forces, and suck out the blood hour after hour, until you see remove the flowing force of the oil; and keep that you do not prick the oil with the points of scalpels, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only pull out those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the oil colic vert and rouge to corrupt what remains of the devil.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you have not power to coil all that in one hour, then do a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains are eased, and be sure that there is an abscess hot, then resume according to this form until he is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the boil of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The arrow is called "arissati" boil: when you cure it with cautery and medicine hot according to what I've said before, and it's not healed, then there is a disease in it that you pierce under the abscess, where it must die, and take out all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackening, if it's in that shape, and they call it "aspère chef", and it's made from a certain iron to fit that form; and pointed as sharp as a lime so as it is now in that present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the bone of the corrupted os, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand until you know that this corruption is healed; and do not do that again, then restore to the leg with medicinal extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the swellings are hot and painful, and the body of the bowel is hot and remains so for 40 days, and does not discharge or swell again, and no accidents happen, it seems that he is healthy; if this is not so, then there is no other engine than to return the fistula to its perforation according to this shape: and when you uncover the bone for the second time with iron, and with medicines sharp, and as soon as it heals uncovered like this, take care of the nails of iron three times at an angle, and let the fist be reduced a little towards the head so that you see well.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put the bone over the shoulder, and withdraw your hand from the oil for a little while, then turn to the whole forest until you pierce the bone and feel that the patient is coming in because he has his hand on his neck; and after restoring the level of dry medicines as I have taught you, if the swelling comes back with the pain, it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the oil's issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are cut wide open, and nothing comes out of the nose or is loosened up, it is advisable to let the patient alone; then apply poultices, then put on bandages with hot wax and herbs to treat, then drain the oil, and apply plaster made of pitch and tar to bind over with strips and cloths; and do so in a manner that you take cloth soft enough, each one doubled four times, and then place one over another according to how much it needs; then strain over a stiff bandage, and reapply the poultices to suck out again; then remove the poultice and let the oil bind tight day and night, and if it gets tied up too tightly, so be it, for now; after a day and a night, oste (remove) the bandages and, if you see the eye healing, this is good; but if not, reapply the poultices and bandages and the bandage again with the poultice until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A piece of torn fabric has fallen out
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the torn fabric comes out, then tears, and brings forth papers like grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see; therefore if you cover your eyes, it is a bad sign that you should insert an needle into the root of the damaged area below what we have discussed above, and then insert another needle with two threads from the side of the skin; pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut off the thread double and tie one part of the torn edge tightly, and tighten well, then pull out the needle, and put on a moist linen cloth soaked in oil, until the thread cuts with the wound, and then treat the wound with soothing things until it is healed; and sometimes the wound is tied by the torn edge each side of a circle of fabric, so that it may be healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes do great appearance, so he must prick at the spot on the nail that comes forth from under the nail, and drive out the moisture with the alum, and descend the eye, and let it enter soon after; then draw it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of oil from the nail
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an oil-filled bow that resembles cold water flowing down, and it's not actually water; and the way of its appearance is such that you must sit the patient upright on a prepared bed and straight, then take hold of the head with both hands two parts, and keep moving it until you see the bow come up to your eyes; then tie it in place, do not let it descend, and if it does not get untangled, know that it's cold water, and if the discharge from the bow is not described as being assembled, as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and put it above the hairy part by the continuation of the conjunctive with the hairy part and the crown, until the bow; and when it is drawn out, then distill into hot oil mixed with honey, or fenugreek boiled with honey, or else be cured with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	we have similar signs of the waters in separation, and that which it is necessary to pierce; if in operation according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary to sit the patient between your hands crossed, with fires of light in front of the sun, and tie up tight the clean oil; then put on one's hand the paper of the oil to one's left hand if their eyes are to the left, or to one's right hand if their eyes are to the right; then take in one's right hand, if their eyes are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or to one's left hand, if their eyes are to the right; then put the tip of the instrument close to the crown by the thickness of a nail in that paper of oil at the inner side of the smaller armillary sphere, and blow the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the paper of oil, and feel that almagda comes to the void; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the end of the measure of the space which is from the plum's joint to the end of the horn; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the hairy part, then put the instrument just there as it is, or near where the oil is, then press out with one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain has come down now, so he sees the patient in front of him and the instrument on his side.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the pain moves down again, put with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and does not move, extract all lightly by turning your hand little by little; and then put back into the oil a little bit of wool gemstone, and clean from within that oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil in a stopper or linen wet with rose oil and plenty of beef fat, and tie it up with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	And so, and for those of our time, let us apply a comfrey brier with plenty of beef fat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the armpit cannot enter into the fat because of its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, so you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", because this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva alone, and do not cut too deeply, but make it subtle, then pour in fat, as we have said; and when you finish the work, instruct the patient to lie down on his back in the dark room; and let him be moved only gently, and give light meals, and do not move his head or arm or hand, and tie him according to his disposition for three days. Then release him from that same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then release him again after seven days; and it is not advisable to do this in the house of treatment or after the incision now, but it is advisable to ease it because the swelling rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the abscessed cauls come, you must free the oil on the seventh day, and the advice of one who sooths an abscess; and when it is eased, then free the eye and put a bandage over it for a day, to be admitted in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then they leave the house a little at a time, and it converts into its case; and you know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Erythraean land, who told us that in some far-off places people made alchemical precipitates, because of which they succeeded with water, but I never saw or knew of it in our land, nor do I find it mentioned in the books of the ancients; and by chance, this may be a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almadah, for those who do not know them will see; and they are of clean wool properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of pus from this same subtlety, and the backside in three angles of anguish.
de la char sor le neis	of gall on the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There is no time when gall-like masses are born or appear in various ways, for there are some that resemble scorpions almost like flies; and if they have such (gall), it has been thickened with fatty color, and then has yellowish gall.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, in case of those gall-like masses that are yellow and not thickened, it is necessary to place the patient on your hands against the sun; open his nostrils, and put the onion on these masses, and draw forth the fumes; for whenever you can sustain that force, take it up at a subtle distance from one part until you know that those gall-like masses are all dried.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be covered, then if you have all the subtle signs and gentle marks present, leave nothing; and if it does not take root, or an abscess forms, cut off as much as is necessary; and if it's malignant pus, hasten to cauterize so that they are not infected and all the bones are properly set, then clean or anoint with wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the pus overflows and moistors come to the face just like to the palace, then know that it is cleansed; and if moistors do not penetrate as it needs, know that there is no marrow in the bone above, by which the signs do not come to bite: therefore it is convenient to put a thread of flax into him in some place, and be careful with hands now, and have between each one some space I must or less; and place the malady's head on the thread as much as possible, and treat smelling until it comes down through the nose into the mouth; and children often do this at schools, and it is a light thing to those who wish to try it; then hold the head that comes by the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and know them one after the other as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct that you do what you know is right for the flesh of the newborn, then take care of the wound, and moisten the child in Egyptian oil, and place them directly under the linen as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments rot all that remains of the flesh; and then put on a linen bandage some days until they are healed, and if it has need of dried medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, because one distills oils and medicines in it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is of silver or lead, like a lantern over, just as a bandage, and conduct it similarly; and if you see one, do so too: make a closed bandage, and let the instruments be ready to purge the head; and hold the hand on the head while we heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the shoulder's cartilage, let the sick one leave it be
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often the head of the new nose grows into a disease called "telul", and it swells and becomes large sores, until it is visible to see; and therefore you should copy at the beginning, and cut through the bone, then apply cautery or hot medicine on it; and if one delays in doing this for too long, when it has become large, if it is hard, he takes a violent cough, of poor smell, of painful breath: do not touch him with iron because it is an enchanted wound, because whenever you cut it once, it brings great evil to the patient; and if the wound is soft by touch, but not by color, and you see that it can be completely covered, then open the sick one and apply the treatment of dried things and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Seeing how much benefit comes from continuing to these worn-out joints, in no case for any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to consider this if it happens to anyone, when he looks at whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adds two layers of flesh to a scar, and cures until he is healed; and if the lips are completely cut off on one side and the other, it is necessary that you burn every part of their hurt until they heal, then reassemble the two lips to a scar, and tie them, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and frankincense crushed; and apply the powders a piece of plaster, hard or any other plaster binding, and let him be until he peels off by himself, and cure with ointment until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch is that you assemble the suture: or by needles, just as we said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the naked hand it goes into the lips abscess, like grains of sand, and small as well as large; therefore you must return to the lips, and cut through each one, and take out with tweezers and clip into each part; then apply the liquid after the vitriol incision breaks, until they are drained; and then wash away the abscess, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	For many times the nose swells when it is closed up, which they call "albulus"; you must hold it in place with the tweezers, and cut at its root, and let the bowel or the wound drain; then put on the patient a vitreous splinter, or other powder constricting and drying; and if that one comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you cut it again, and cauterize: if it does not come back after the cautery; and these are the forms of oozing to cover.
des sordens	from the dirt
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no times that the teeth are assembled at the top of the bones, inside the mouth between the gums, warts that are ugly and painful; and there is no time when a black and yellow tooth and worm appear, until corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes putrid; you must sit the patient in your hands, so his wounds may be visible, until nothing remains; and thus do white and green, and yellow and other colors, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at first sight, it's good; but if not, it resumes on the second day and the third time, until you have all; and know that teeth need different forms of oozing to clean, according to what the work shows, because the rasps for cleaning teeth have different shapes than those for teeth between the gums; and these forms and others should be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay the treatment as long as you can, for this should not be done in no way; because it is a very high substance, therefore we have no excuse to fear.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you are certain about the state of the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain is in the patient, and consider it to be or of a good tooth, and treat the good tooth; and see that they do not depart from the pain for this reason, until the bad one is removed, because we have never wanted to do so by these physicians; and when you are certain about the state of the tooth, it is necessary that you scorch around the tooth on all sides with a sharp instrument very strongly to ward off the gums from all parts; then you should mow it down with your teeth or use fine pincers at the first point and point, until it is well cleaned, and then firmly fix the pincers; and tie the patient's teeth between your own shoulders, and their good tooth so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth directly towards the broken side, and if it does not jump forth, take out any of these instruments and gently pour it into each part lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perforated and infected, it is fitting that you fill them with cloths, to where the holes are; and if you tighten them subtly with forceps, so that they do not break when tightening; and it is good to be cautious over the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And carefully watch so that you do not break it, and leave some of it behind, and tell the patient by the illness of the root for greater pains at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And watch that you do not make it as the ignorant doctors do, who by their haste and boldness break a chariot every time, and bring in nothing like what we have told you; but sometimes they come by the ointment of this great sickness because of the roots that remain, or because they break the chariot, just as has happened to us often; and when the tooth is strong, wash it with wine or ash or vinegar; and if blood comes, which happens often, apply a splinter of vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the splinters, when they are not pulled out with the tooth first, should be long points and thick handles, so that they do not double back when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be thick members that do not bend when pulled out, and are made of iron well made, and have teeth to hold them in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling out, it is necessary to put a moist cotton on the wound with butter once or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is moistened, because then you put on the tongs called "algefri", for which the cut seems like a bee sting; and they are made thus as a file, and it's this form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge at all these tenacious attachments, it is fitting that you uncover the whole chariot around the root, and place the instrument which is called "althali", namely plainer, so that this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And so even if it is great and severe, and the root does not break, but rather jumps through it, that's good; but if that's not the case, then help with all the instruments, for the forms will come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you assist from this instrument that has two roots, for it is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the root of the teeth, and from this instrument which resembles great pincers, for it is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be used so that it will not break, and you know that many instruments of bone are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtle try for themselves their own instrument, according to what his works and the illness show him, because he has found in some cases illnesses where the ancient do not teach an instrument for the diversity of these things and since it will break on the chariot or on another bone if you do not search for instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and help with gestures, because this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting, in order to hold the bone firmly, but not so tightly that it can't be removed; and then put back in the patient as much medicine as is fitting for him, and if there is decay in the bone, which is small, so that the instrument will reach into it.
