Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not as it should be according to its natural body form, and its shape is ugly, and in young girls so much so that you must know if the teeth are new after the tooth, and they are not in their right place, and you cannot adjust or bind them: then take a rasp; and if it's around with the tooth, take this instrument which has the form described here, and it is similar to a small beak, and it is made of good iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the rasp is a small, small tool in your hands each day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the other teeth; if it appears that we can bind it, take some powdered lime, as is its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the lime from which we make needles; and in lime the tooth is pounded a little bit each day lightly in your hands, so that it does not move until it breaks; then the plane is at the end of all the rasps, and if the teeth are too pointed, then it is binding the roughness so that it becomes even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the words.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose, or by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press up on that which it hurts so much that it will break, and you cure them with medicines restricting, but it is not effective; if they must be restrained with a thread of gold, because the threads of silver turn green and rot, but the gold does not move at all; and if the thread is neither too thin nor too thick, nor too small, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are falling out, take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then put the pins between the teeth of yours, if there are one or more, until you see correctly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering from where you started, and strain your hand carefully and gently, until it does not move at all; and let your tie be gentle to the root of the tooth so that it will not escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the head of the shoulder to be cut with a thread at a pair of pliers, and assemble it, and put it between the healthy teeth, and set it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then let it stay thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes loose, or the thread breaks, take hold of another thread; if it remains and serves thus for its time, and this is the shape of the dens and the figure of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, as fresh as fresh, just like we have said; and do not let anyone else touch who is not skilled and experienced, because at no time should you make a form of a bone-like tooth, and put it in the place where it is missing, and hold it tight as we have said; and keep it there and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cover the joint of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no joint that comes from under the tongue or is born that way; rather it happens so. Either by accident of a wound healed; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, put their head on your healthy one, and lift their tongue; then cut the nerve around the large part until the tongue is loosed from its place, and if it has hardened or not, and this happens due to sudden bleeding, insert the needle and cut around the large joint; and be careful that the wound not be too deep by the artery below; and when you have done so, put the injured one in warm rosewater and ash, or cold water, then put a piece of linen under the tongue; and bind each night with a bandage until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And when the vein comes open, if it is covered with vitriol, break on the arm; and if not, cauterize at the fire cautery, which is good for this; then apply another remedy until he becomes healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it to be in the shape of pus, whether yellow or black or hard, because if he does not feel pain and you do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it inclines towards blisters, and there is moisture, then remove the ulcer, and let them make one with a small spatula, and deliver from both sides; and if he does not feel pain at your work, put vitriol on the area so that he becomes stained, then return to his work until all is done; then lift the limb gently and carefully, and apply other remedies until he becomes healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	there is no time inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called amandres, and when you cure them, just as we said in division, if they are not healed, be cautious: if it is a hard abscess of small sensation and red flesh, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is red and the root is big, do not touch with iron, because of the worsening of blood loss; but let it be so long as it does not die, and then you will cut it off, or it would break on its own; and if it has a white color, and the root is subtle, tie the instrument to cover it, but first look carefully whether the abscesses are closed and have subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And then instruct the patient to sit in front of the sun, and their joints should be healthy, and he will operate the mouth and the surgeon will press the serjeant between his hands, and push the tongue downward towards all the instrument, for this is the form; and it shall be made either from silver or fine gold just like our scales:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue towards all this instrument, and see the abscess, if one takes the onion and pokes it in the honeycomb, and pulls the thread up higher than you can; and pull no other thing from the cloth, then cut at the instrument, for this is the form that looks like force; and look at how the head is curved, and one point bent towards another, and are very good, and made of iron or tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, then grab the tongs, because it is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And so cutting from one side and the other side; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after incising gargarize the patient with hot cold water, and hot and easy, and if blood has come out, then gargarize the patient with vinegar or pomace of pomegranates cooked or infusions of myrtle, and similar things, until the veins are tied off; then do the cure until he is cured; and sometimes new abscesses appear in the throat beyond the two almonds, so cut them now as you did the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was nestled in the throat, to wit, the small abscess; and I had tightly closed the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked conduit, nor eat or drink, and she died if she stayed like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the swellings were high enough that two poultices had been applied twice to each of the two wounds near the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Therefore I gave him a poultice and applied one to each of the two wounds near the neck, then he was burned with fire, and a large portion of a bow was used. Then another poultice was applied to the other wound, and his throat was closed and his tongue pressed; after that a poultice was placed on the swelling, and a part of it was cut away, and only a little blood came out; and so I opened up the conduct of the throat for the woman, and since then she began to drink cold water and wine, and did not stop cutting at the swelling for a long time; and the swelling kept recurring, and filled with pus that had been emptied from me, until it became quite large; therefore I inserted and cauterized inside the throat: thus he remained still for some time, and I departed from these parts, and left God to care for him after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the humors descend to the eye and it is pulled down and lengthened, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and rounded, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the pus is healed, and it is subtle, so it is fitting to copy it; and the one that is rounded and not long, will not assemble and is not suitable for an incision; and if it is red or of flesh color or black, then it is necessary to remove the incision from it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have told, of its bluntness and length, that you set the patient on his side in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we mentioned earlier; then poke a needle into the eye, and remove it from under, and cut at both ends as I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the physician to cut no more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until she is sane.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, it is advisable to use an instrument at the cautery of their fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is cool water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your sound one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we have said in the cautery chapter, and mixes it with cool running water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and using the tip of this instrument, as it forms:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let a hair or nail on his head be touched with the medicine, like the servants of a spoon, and place the instrument on top of the nose; and if the patient sits on his chest, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, which does not fall down the throat, nor the breath; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the nose, for half the quantity of an hour, until you see the blood come out and the bites of the medicine be stopped; and if you see, take cotton and wipe it above any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into a can with cotton inside, until the cotton is on the nose; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and after four days or five, if you have need to restart the cauterization of the medicine, so restart it, and after the cautery clean it with vinegar water, and cure gargling until he is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery, whether it's done with incision or fire; if it's cured according to this manner, take camphor and myrrh and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them together in a pot, and put it on easily, and boil; and the pots should be well-glazed with hot earth, and with instruments of the head according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And if it is of silver or lead, and one of the nails is inserted into the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is numbed; afterwards, repeat often, until the eye dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess hot, for many things happen, and do it only at the declination of the abscess hot.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a nail and put it inside the head with a small piece of iron, so that the patient's mouth does not feel too hot; because the iron does not weigh down the vapor in the mouth, and this is a good cure for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often when a sword is pressed against the throat of a person or an arrow of fish, or anything else; so it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun until all the instrument, so that you can see what is being done; and if something does not come out and returns to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit so that the meat will be cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing gets burned from vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a root of lettuce, or a dry piece of bread; and tie it with the string, and then apply glue; and when it comes to life again, you will extract the venom; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument from the plunger according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the patient to let the strumens curve upwards at the head if it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head up higher; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it comes alive, or do not force the bone inside; and make sure that the patient is willing to swallow the instrument, for this will prevent them from having an ulcer, or pushing the bone into their throat; if they swallow, or take it for all the instrument at once, so that it is evenly distributed.
de la sansue de la gorge	Concerning the strumens of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the strumens of the throat medicated, as I have said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look into the patient's throat in the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see an abscess, if it has one small ulcer, or have fine nails that are worth the same.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If it's not worth it, take a hot iron shank and plunge it into the neck of the sick person, then swallow or cut off some of the iron.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient has fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full draught of cold water, and cover the mouth, and swallow in that direction, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the abscess feels the pain, he vomits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not vomit as we have said, then perfume the sick person with asafoetida in the instrument that I have mentioned for the inhalation of the wound; do this many times, because it will cause him to pass tar-like.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Instruct the patient to put a pot with charcoal and wood chips in the middle, and let the instrument's nails protrude from it. Then, make a fumigation, and have the patient put the head of the cane in their mouth, close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to there; and now the cough will come, and if she doesn't cough, then repeat the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient with thirst, and eat foul things and ashes, and do not drink water at all; and thus the disease will be overcome by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument for treating an abscess is such that when you can see it, it looks like curved tongs with nails entering into the neck; and has the appearance of a beak, and has roughness of lime, so that what she takes, it cannot be loosened; and thus it appears:
li chapistres des apostemes	The medical practitioners of this art
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what is remembered afterwards in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways of doing it, one of which is in its own likeness, and because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for them to be inside or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses on the head are different from those on the chest, and the abscesses on the liver are different from those that occur in joints, each having its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses where one should not pierce until the bowel is fully dead according to its completion; and if some have them that it must be pierced when they seem cured, but do not die according to their completion, such as those near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For in the abscess when it comes from the joints and is left until it is swollen, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, because that is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is at the main limb and if you delay the perforation until it dries up, so that it does not harm the principal limb; or if it is at the foundation, if you pierce it so that it dies; and it should not be done to pierce an abscess when one thinks the digestion is completed, because fires in which there is a wound from the foundation, will make it worse by bursting into more, and forming a fistula; and cannot be cured with great delay.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is fitting that you know the size of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to the completion, and this is when the pain is assuaged, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the diminishment of the swelling and the quickening of the head of the abscess, and all the other signs; it is fitting that you make the perforation as far down as possible from the abscess, depending on where it opens up, and so the perforation be long in the body, and if the abscesses are at hands or feet, or joints, nerves, arteries, or at those places which are equalized with no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When these are swollen, according to the state of the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the charnel cavity, if it must be cut so that you leave the perforation until confirmed to be completed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front, the body will be filled with the poison from it, and it is full of much filth; and by chance, the lips and the soles of your feet may become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that must be cut according to the size of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting to treat small abscesses with small perforations; and large abscesses with large perforations, and many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is suitable to stitch them up, and cover them, when they have become as soft as a cloth, and are softened, then it is fitting to do so as we make for the baby: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and those whose perforation is like the beak of myrtle, like abscesses of angles; and if there are others where one makes a round size, and other sizes and shapes of perforations.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	In those who do not have a head, as with an abscess that is superficial, it is necessary to pierce them plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much blood, and you pierce, if you take out all of the blood in that hour, but take only one part; then stop the abscess just at dawn on the next day, then do not touch anything underneath; do this many times with great care, until the bowels are all cleaned out; meanwhile, if the patient has weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a child, or an old man who is decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But the expectation is that there will be no great recovery either with the issue of the blood, so that by chance the patient may die, and you should not despair.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instructs then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if it is a wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is an open cut, then attempt to close it with linen or old cotton; and if there are great wounds, and many are punctured, then it is advisable that you insert one tent in each so that they come into contact with each other; and if you have pierced the abscess a part of the skin, and you have tied it around, then it is advisable to fill it up with old cotton or rasps of linen soaked in moisture, and tie it up just as often; then apply, and treat with ointment until it is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood comes from your wound, then apply cold and clear water, and moisten it with a cloth, and cover the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to persevere with bloodletting if they do not succumb, and follow the government and treatment, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, if it is during winter, and if the poultices are applied to the abscesses, take care to put on wet tents and drapes made of wine and oil; and if it is dry, and the poultices are applied, take care to apply wet drapes made of water and oil, or in wine and oil boiled, just one day after, as we have said; and then uncover the abscesses and wash and cure, as it seems necessary, until they are sane.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is true, universally in the treatment of abscesses: where you have said how to apply before the treatments for abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For those who come from the head with small abscesses, and are many of the kind that are in cloth, just as the jarter of a goat, and much so there is similar appearance.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also grasses and things like which there is moisture just as with feet; and some of the kinds that are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause them harm.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the wounds of the groin if you are experienced with all instruments that are called "entromissoire", because the form comes after this, what kind of thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	Because if it contains moisture, they cut from above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, so scorch without leaving any of that skin which contains the moisture, for it will return again when you leave nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise, in water and cloth, apply to the wound, and let it rest on the other day; and those who are left overnight will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, if you continue the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the linen, until you know well that it will not stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for him, so he becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold tightly within no meat, if you cut according to this form, long and straight; then take your knife, and scrape all over, and apply all your cure of treating for the place where it is; and if the arteries cause a contrary effect, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And as for the abscess if it is a stone, and on cutting and on treating so as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut above the stone abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because it has little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or joints have no moisture, and such as I copied or cut in the chest of an old woman; and found the abscess just like a hard stone rough and white, which could not be broken; and if anyone had struck it with fire, one would have done equally well to make a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or joints, whether those which come on the chest or near the children's ears and their rootlets, cut them open so they always go out to the nose; and treat as it requires.
des scrophules	There are swellings
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	This occurs frequently in the neck, and under the armpits, and inside the groin, and sometimes occur elsewhere on the body, and are very painful, and are joined together one by another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each swelling is properly located in its own place, as if the lump and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the signs of these swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are swellings that contain moisture, and those that are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then, where you see a good disposition in the groin area, and it resembles the color of the body, and is silent from all parts and is not reddened around the neck or artery or vein, and is not deep; it is fitting to copy it from above, and scorch from each part, and make the two lips red like wounds, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and cut little by little, and be sure that you will not copy the nerve or vein, and do not scratch with sharp instruments, lest your hand gets injured, and you see too far ahead, that you may copy only what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	Instruct the patient to let the vein or artery be opened, and if it will not stay open, put vitriol in the wound, or some powder that stays blood, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess is eased and the pain is mellowed, and begin to cauterize.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is not bled, so that it returns to your body, complete as much as you can; then see if there are no small swellings, if cut them and lance.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a great quantity of blood in the root of the swelling vein, it is not advisable to cut that vein at its root, but tie with a strong double thread, and let fall as much as possible without pain; then apply the wound with Egyptian ointment, and cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you strike the entire skull, it is fitting that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and the sutures now, so that there is no remaining swelling from the great size of the skull.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is fitting that you understand to strike the root of the nail, and to treat the flesh, and the sutures as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those skulls that hold superfluous matter, pierce at the top or it bursts open; and pierce as previously stated, in dependence, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of corruption is eradicated; and when the wound is well cleaned, the treatment of ointment will heal until it is fully recovered.
de squinance	of squamousness
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old people spoke and said about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	It is necessary for those who have laryngitis that the cut of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and one should not give aid to this because all veins and the flesh are swollen in the patient where there is an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the lungs.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the flesh, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three circles or four small cuts across the middle, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut through the cartilage; and that is convenient because there is no cartilage and the vessels are long to be inquired.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the masters to extend the skin of the neck to its full extent, then cut through the vein until it comes to the jugular; and release the vasa sanguinis, if you see anything, and then strike at the sac, as we have said; and this will be proven by the section of the femoral vein that springs from the broken limb, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound covered with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound of the vein, and clean the entire surface to the cartilage; then administer medicines that make urine flow, until it is purified.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Bleeding from the nostrils should not be attempted unless the throat is completely frozen, and the patient is pronounced dead, and the abscess has broken.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Adonques cope on the epiglote because the patient cannot bear, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four, then they ordered that the wound be sewn up and cured, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and struck it against her throat, and cut some of the fatty tissue on her neck; and I was called to cure her, and found her dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found out that blood had come from it, and I realized she had not cut the vein or a vein was forced to do so through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have fallen ill and sewn up the wound and treated it until it was healed; and it did not happen to the young woman that she would be red in her throat, and return after her disposition; therefore I say that there is no fear of strangulation in the epiglottis sewing.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts or abscesses are called "hernia of the throat", and they are large cysts in the color of a jet, and are often found in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no inflammation.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is in two forms, because one is like fat tissue, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear of it, and should not be treated with fire, only for those who are small, and examine him carefully from head to toe: if you find it also as fat tissue, and have no sign or reason, cut it out just like one cuts us, and remove all its cover, if there's nothing left; and search thoroughly, and treat it as needed, until he is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of us, and I will say all the similarities; and it is necessary that I tell you the whole difference between us and the opposite.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever is when and inflammation remains, as long as the heat has not passed and it has been accomplished to purify; then rests the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	The opposite does not have heat or fever or pain, and contains the spleen, which is its own sac and resembles its body color, and begins to swell like a bladder, and becomes of similar size and consistency; and has colors, or thicknesses, or moistness, and much in it like what I have said in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the opposite, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument called "entremissoire", according to its form whether it is a chapter or after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Instruct the manner of extracting pus from an abscess is to take up more moist than you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs a little by little until you know that the contents have pierced the vein, then extract the intervening stuff, and be careful so it doesn't burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture from the cut is as clear as when you extracted pus from other abscesses; and if there is no more moisture coming out after removing the intervening stuff, then know that it is fatty, so mark it with a cross, and take it by pinches, and lightly scrape off each part, watching where you go to clean the wound so you can bring it back to health with the nail; and if you cannot bring it back to health, extract it in pieces, as long as there is nothing left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays in place, it will return to its previous state many times; and if it remains for a little while without causing harm, then apply the wound with some corrosive powders, bind the wound, and put on soothing substances over the abscessed area, and cure with other cures until he is healed; and if the joint is swollen, cut off two fingers from the wound, and cure the one who is causing inflammation.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is inflamed against this or another thing, which you hasten and apply with the vitriol solution, and let it remain for two days or three, until the wound is clean, then return to cover what was left untouched.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of internal strumous interjections, and they come in three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and among them there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like the needles used for suturing the suture, made of citron wood, iron, or silver, which are yellow in color, and more effective at plugging deep black holes for closing corsets of fistulas; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the lacerations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are of much resemblance, as you see here: great, medium-sized, and small; and so too have ulcers with two heads in three different manners; and so too have ulcers with three heads, and are also of three manners; and so too have ulcers with two heads, and a single head only, and are of three manners; and all this is necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these (wounds) are cut in such a way that they are sharp-edged, and there are some that do not cut through more than one side, because of which the skin is scorched, so that you do not cut into the vein or the nerve; and these deep-seated ones have ulcers returned to their original place in the palm of the hand, so that the patient does not lose any limb at the opening of the abscess; and they come in three manners: great, small, and medium-sized, as you see; and one should not use more than necessary just for the wooden splint, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groin, and similar limbs; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling the scabs of fistulas, according to this shape, because bloodletting is done.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and place it in no case on a limb that is whole, which has been bled and has arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, if he thinks it is fitting according to this form, follows this line from .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then bring together the two lips of the wound on a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if the breast droops down, and becomes small like those of women, so that it hangs from two seams like torn flesh: because one might stay attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from .b. to .g.; then scrape the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powder, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or if the incision has not been fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the corruption of blood, if it seems fitting that you fill the wound with wet cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it finishes the remaining fat, then cure until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The evacuation of blood when opening a vein
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	There are cysts that come from the armpits which are hard and have boils or cracks, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those which contain moisture should be closed according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bow (tissue) inside the abscess is emptied, apply the treatment of old cloth to the wound and leave it on for the next day, then remove all the cloth, and treat with ointment as needed until the wound heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to boils, then cut as we have said in cutting boils, and if the wound is closed with tissue, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the artery's cutting
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is sewn up on top, if it often comes to an abscess, then also it happens that a vein is swollen and an abscess; and if one constrains in such a way as to be for the artery, then it has long abscesses because of it; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel strangulation; and when it's for the vein, it is difficult to find; and it's foolishness to cover this abscess, and especially when it is in the lower parts such as the groin and the armpits and near the neck and full of other foul things, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to cure with iron, and one who has a head must also be cured in the same way, and for one who has swelling of an artery make it above the skin; then work on the chest as much as possible, and cut open the vein so that it is visible; then insert an arrow into the vein below where the arrow was inserted, and tie off the vein with a double thread in two fingers, according to what I have taught you when extracting two arteries from the temples; then tie the patient with a strap around his neck until he no longer has any swelling; and cure him as is fitting for that, so long as he is healthy; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, it is necessary to sew it up by hand as much as you can from one end to the other; then insert a new arrow into the place where you are sewing, and tie the thread on both sides in four fingers; then cut off the swelling so that there may be some issue; then cut off the swelling with care and leave what is tied; then put up a soft bandage soaked in wine and oil, and thus cure him with tentes and ointments until he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	The movement of pus from a boil
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	And when pus comes into an artery and a vein, it comes from boils when they are dry, or because of excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows, where there are joints, and it's a source of pus, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is associated with many deaths; and when it's strained, it feels pain to the patient, and isn't entirely absent from the body, but rather under the skin; and it mutates in all parts, and doesn't move forward or backward, neither above nor below, and those who have joints cannot cover them with iron: by chance they may contract the disease; and those who are on their head or forehead, apply the cupping to the spatulate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have a pair of tongs, and cut it at its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it on an onion, and scorch it, then clean and remove the bone, and assemble the wound to the shoulder, and the cure until he is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of great mouths hanging downwards.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is no time for the intestines and it has no other part affected, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its appearance, and it has subtle roots, and large stones; and there are small ones and large ones; I saw one person who had two intestines that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were partially split open, and decayed due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I have copied them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI., and the wounds in the incision are such that you should look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the arthritic joint is pale and moist with subtle root; then cut at the spatulate large, and be present with the cautery on fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	But when cutting comes many times with large bleeding from the cut, and if you do not wait for the cautery, then hasten then; and if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision on fire, take a well-made thread and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it two days; and then bind it, and cease to strain the thread until it cuts the joint, and work with it bit by bit; and if the roots are thick, then fear cutting yourself for the belly, but you can cut half of it, then cautery that he does not bleed again; then cure the wound, and make sure that you do not cut the tendons which are of fleshy color and poor sense and eye-red.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchanted abscess, and I have come to this treatment of canker after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the swollen lump swells up.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the lump comes from cauterizing an open wound or cutting through a split in a vein, and it is on the belly with some boils, as it happens in other kinds of wounds, such as when veins are cut or arteries are pricked according to what lies ahead, or due to windiness; and if this is due to the cut through the vein and from the swelling, then the color of the abscess looks like the color of the body, and it's a light-colored thing with pain, and opens up in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's from the intestines, then it's more diverse, and when you press on both sides, but it comes back again, and by chance it is hardened, and becomes much larger at the entrance of the bath and due to great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit. Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting that you leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Because of doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is concerning the intestine or the gallbladder, then it is fitting to instruct the patient to tie his ankle, and have him lie straight down, then stitch all around the wound; then command him to lie in your hands, then go towards the place you marked earlier with a splint; then make half of the incision on top of the entire inch; then tie it around with a strong thread or cord firmly, and leave loose like that; then open the upper part of the incision and pour in your thumb's index, and look at the intestine; if you find the thread caught, release it, and pour the intestine into the empty stomach; and if you find the gallbladder, tie it up with an inch, and cut its superfluity; and if the vein makes a contrary effect, or the vein, then go straight in, and return to your work and take two sharp needles, and pierce them through as we made before; then strain the incision for four leus on top of the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the patient until it heals itself; or tie that dead thing back with a thread when it is close to death; or when it happens to die suddenly, cut it according to what is needed, and stitch the incision as we have said; and take out the sanc or moisture that you find, then cure the patient of what he needs, and heal his wound.
dou chancre	There is a sore.
