Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the similarities of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron treatment; and we say that chancre is contagious in the nipple, and there is great care in its cure; and the ancients said that when chancres are on you or can be scraped off like chancer on a nipple, and in similar places, and all these must be removed when it begins to start; and when they become large and old, it does not seem wise to approach them, because I have never found anyone who has been cured by me, nor has any one ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is in the place where you can remove it, as we have said, it is that you do not purify the patient of black bile once; then make the patient healthy if he has manifest signs of repletion; then make the patient well for making an ulcer; then apply your poultices or chancre, and wash off all parts, and leave nothing on the bone; and let the wound heal completely, and expect that the patient will be safe to your hands or with anything; but if the blood flows from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until it is stained, then cure with another treatment until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	For we have said in the division of these symptoms of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each symptom, and the treatment that is done by medicines, and the one that is cured by iron: if only it is cut; and you should not touch with iron in these two symptoms: this is to say, tympanites and yposarche, because they are a deadly thing; therefore when you treat the medicine for this symptom of dropsy which is called "eclites" from medicines, and the cure does not profit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as constipation and solution of the stomach and similar things; do not touch with iron because there is doubt; and if you see the patient very robust and only suffers from dropsy alone, and he is neither too old nor too young, do thus: lift the patient straight up onto your hands, and the ministers press the belly towards the bottom of the feet, then take the spatumile with thorny ends according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so we turn to two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pointing and cutting must be done carefully so that he does not penetrate the intestine when it is inserted; and you cannot stop bleeding. Then examine if the drooping (of blood) has been attached to the intestines: if it is advisable, cut under the third joint of the bowels downward on the outer side of the nail; and if the drooping is due to liver disease, then cut on the left side of the third joint; and if it is for the muscles, then on the right side; but it must not be that the patient lies on the wound so that the humors flow to the weak part; then puncture all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and raise your hand to the length of the sheath between the skin and the scabbard just as you are scraping when reaching the quantity of an acorn or less in passing; then puncture the scabbard until the sheath comes to life for him, that is the measure of the water, then remove it, and insert this instrument which is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it appears like a silver chain with subtle rings, and is made of iron or horseshoe leather, and has small holes in that area; on one side there are three holes; on the other side two holes; and on another side one hole; and the nails are cut as thin as a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes shape like a pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	On the top of it is a small nail, so that when instruments come to water, now take them up from there; empty then half or one-third of it, because if you empty more than it needs in that hour, by chance he may die from the release of his spirit of the weapon, or he will throw his hands or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue signify for the sick person, and their pulse; then take up the instrument and hold back the water, because it is now held by the nail that is on the syphilitic spot, as I have said, so you must pierce according to this manner; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering such, and take off a small quantity of water; do not do this on any one day, and be cautious not to go mad until he does not stay but for a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you are in doubt about the patient, and let them drink much water, so that the cure makes a poultice of earth or hot sand, and stays with it for a long time or takes a bath and stands under the sun, and if they drink of wine; and the cure gives to medicines desiccative until the patient is healthy, and cauterizes on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There are no children born without a wart on the penis, or if there is one it's small, or if not it's out of place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If they want it to pierce immediately, so that they can penetrate anywhere in the short span of time with such subtlety:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to put on a cloth soaked in onion over their nose and mouth, and tie it tightly three times a day or four times a day, and when they wish to urinate, do not open the wound, but rather let the urine come out, and then remove the dressing; and by chance, if no discharge comes, because the urine that arrives does not allow the wounds to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If this is an opening in the foot, treat it with onion, as we have said, and it will spread.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in their own foot are afflicted, because those who have an opening in the head of the penis cannot urinate until they lift their penis up high; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come down to the anus, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to lie on his back, then stretch out his arm and strike it with the end of a spear as long as that of an arrow, in such a way that the wound is inflicted in the middle. And be careful not to cause excessive bleeding which comes many times, and if there is bleeding, then bandage the one who bleeds so that they do not bleed again, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from boils of the arm
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times boils come to the arm, and it is an ugly appearance; and some are malignant and not malignant; if you wish to prick them at once with a needle, strike them and lance all of them, then put on cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure with a fine knife until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the skin is malignant, of purple color and swollen, then it is fitting that you apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you cut it, and if the skin is in a swollen state, both inside and outside the flesh, then it is fitting to remove the swelling that is inside first, and when it is heated, if the cure heals.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	But when you cure it together, if you are not certain that the swollen part of the vein will be cut out, and blackness and corruption appear in its place, and at what time; then it is fitting to take away all that which is black and corrupted, and cover it with a plaster made from honey and flour, made from the rind of green pomegranates and vinegar, and cure other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a bloody purulence comes, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is applied in two ways: this means that when there is discharge and corruption, and if the head of the vein has dried up and contracted, it is advisable to cut out or remove some part of the vein, and let the patient pass urine; and when the hair grows again on the head of the vein which has not been circumcised, either because of a wound or an abscess, it is then advisable to burn with a sharp instrument the skin around the neck, until the ligaments are released, and the head of the vein is delivered from all parts; and if this is painful to devise, then it is advisable to burn it at the upper end of the vein and the hair, with a spatumile (a small flat tool) soaked in vinegar and oil, in between two layers, so that it does not become inflamed again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not free from further complications if it were to continue like other wounds; every way we do this work of our willpower, and specifically on children, because it is a necessary task that we must perform the better work, and the more gentle for safety.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not tell the ancient people about circumcision for their children because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greatest part of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision in order to learn from them, and gained experience, but the authorities were opposed because it involved two tools, and by chance some people died from above and others below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery covers it, and the pain is double, and at the purification which is done with a great deal of uncertainty about the point of the member; and at the purification of the ulcer by chance escapes the iron, and runs over the wound, and often comes to this as if they needed no further purification and I have seen that.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification that is made with force, I have found the good fortune of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, it cuts exactly the same way in both direction; but if the thread is not very tight around the skin; and so happens that the first operation should be done as if you were thinking of a child, so that you do not make any further movements than to tie the thread around the horn just enough, and then let it go in all kinds of ways that you can; then take it straight into your hands, and keep the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see, nor any other symptoms; then put your hand on the horn and blow on it, and take it up high until the cut is made; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there; then tie the second thread around it with a double string; then tie it under both at once; and hold it tight as much as you can for two fingers' length, then take the head off the horn's end; then let the blood flow little by little because it’s drying; and put powder on top and on the powder that is glued to the ointment of a rose-water mixed with oil roasted well, and confit with good olive oil and fresh, and leave it up to the other day, and cure him again for as long as he is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force at purification is this: the two shoulders are joined and must be tightened and shortened, and the shoulder is as large as the other equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the edges within are split at the incision; therefore it must be extended to your joint, so that they make an opening; and it is done equally, and if you cannot hold to your joint, then take your nails, and then strike.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it is three days and the thing below the vein is swollen, leave it until the edges of the wound are smoothed out and lightly scrape it; strike as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the vein, for it will not harm a bit.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wounded limb of sudden pain with powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if one strikes out of measure over it, and it goes to the top, so that it does not harm; cure then, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	And retention of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stone, or blood congealed, or bowels, or stones, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that it is blocked by a stone which is stuck or wedged at the junction of the bladder and the colon, so that it is advisable to lower the patient's knees. And place their feet on their back, and stretch out their belly from above the back, and constrain the patient as much as possible; and afterwards the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone upwards, because the urine flows freely; and if not, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, so it is advisable to administer extraction for all the instruments called "siringue", which are made like this: they should be made of fine silver, light, and delicate, like a bird's feather; and should be cylindrical, half a palm long, and subtle in shape.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Instruct the patient to take twice as much fil (likely a medicinal powder or ointment), and tie a piece of linen cloth or cotton around their head; then pour the fil into the vein. Then cut off the excess linen and pour it back into the head of the vein, afterwards anoint the vein with oil or butter and juniper berries; put the patient on the couch, and lift up the bladder and the uterus with olive oil moistened and olive oil and cold water; then gently insert the vein into the uterus, until it reaches the root of the uterus, then double the vein upwards towards the bowels; afterwards pour the vein before reaching the bladder, and listen to the patient feeling it coming out through a void place, because if the conduit is twisted there, that’s not done according to this order, but due to the way it moves in there. Then tie the thread with all the linen cloth little by little, and let the urine follow the linen, afterwards take it out, and pour the urine; and reinsert the vein until the bladder is empty, and relieve the patient's pain.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is assembled, and you see the water and medicine distill, do this to all the instrument called "clepsedre", and it's in this shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if it has three punctures: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the medicinal powder is put close to the tip so that it cools well the urethral passage, if possible to treat moisture, and push when necessary. When you see pouring your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the container in the moisture, and pull out what is inside; pulling out the moisture from the container, then push the container hard again; if the moisture enters again, it will be in the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of a cystoscope which they use to clog the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et is of silver or iron and the nails are higher; and below it in the groin where the ligaments split; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see clumping up the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat it over the fire; then pour the head into the blister in the neck, then strain your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the clot has come to the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle and puncture it round about; then pour the strong thread into those wounds, then assemble the circle as one would assemble the nail, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division how to cut stones and extract medicines; and I have told the difference between stone jasper and rainstones, and all the signs, and when which stone one should operate on with scaling; and in the vessel and phallus; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone jasper in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that urine suddenly escapes from the bladder like water escaping in its subtlety; and it opens up the veins, and scratches the patient's phallus, and he pricks him many times, and then becomes inflamed; and because of this, there are many openings; and lightens up the children until they are 4 years old; is very heavy in the elderly, and is like being middle-aged, for those who are between middle age and old age; and is easier to cure for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we arrive at the cure, it is necessary to first clean the patient with lye, for to remove all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But it is not necessary every time to cut into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the arms, and push down and move away from below, so that the stone comes out to the bottom of the bladder, and does not fall again up into him; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be below his knees, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then take it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, immediately hasten now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not come out at the touchstone to its entirety, moisten your right index finger with oil from your left hand, since the patient is diseased or in your left side, since the patient is a youth unfulfilled; and pour it into his fundament, and take the stone, and when you feel it on your right, if it clings to the neck of the bladder; then press on your right finger, and pour it out at the void where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to stretch out his right hand fingers towards the top, and his left hand palm the skin below the fingers in the part where one makes the incision; then pour the spatulate mixture, for this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Make it between the tendons and the foundation, not in the middle but on the left side of the nail; and it should be straight under the stone, and both ends towards the foundation, and it should make an incision to traverse if it is wide by chance, without being too big; inside it is narrow, according to the size of the stone, neither too great; in case the pressure hits one that is on the foundation, it may jump out for lack of work; and know that there are pieces of stone or angles, and edges: if they are rough to come out; and if there's some that are low, like a splinter, and rounded, from which the exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it must be covered, and a greater wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out again because of the pain that the pain relievers cannot alleviate; but strive with effort to treat, or to cauterize with tongs, until you have removed it by pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound ointment of enchanter's plant and dragon's blood, and bind, and put above a moist cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water cold and hot, to calm the inflammation; then revive the patient under his neck, and do not untie the band for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, give him much oil and water to drink; then apply the oil of defenicon and basilicon, until he is cured.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Et if the abscesses come into the wound and cause corrosion, and congealment of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this means that without urination: put then your fingers into the wound, and extract that wound, because if they remain, the bladder will corrode and rot; then lift the wound with water and oil and cloth, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is fitting that all the wounds you cure, you tie up the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra, and fixed there, and the urine cannot come out; then, if you are told this by another, that you measure the height often, you excuse yourself from this measurement for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tried this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Before I apply iron according to this form and fix it at three angles in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the string and put it around the vein below the stone, if it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the iron into the vein lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the iron to your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if it comes soon afterwards, then press your hand on that which is left behind of the stone inside the vein.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken and comes out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then put the string below the stone and the other above, then make the vein straight to the stone between the two strings, then pull it out, and release the string, and clean the wound frozen up in the injury; and cure until he is well.
de la piere des femmes	Of stones from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is no chance that stones are found in women, and if they occur once, the cure will be troubled, and is prohibited for three reasons: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that we cannot find any woman who knows how to shave her stones herself, especially when she is cast.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the fourth reason is that in this art of hands you cannot find a woman who knows; and the fifth reason is that the stones from women are more embedded than those from men, because it can be made into a deeper pit, and great fear there is. And if necessity arises for this, it is necessary to take a midwife well knowing, and at pains to reach it, and if you do not find her, do not choose a subtle deceit; and present the maiden well-versed in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to make what you command from the inquiry of the stone; and look very carefully whether she is a virgin: then it is necessary to put on the seal or foundation and seek for the stone; and if she finds it, she will constrain herself under the seal, and demand that she pour the seal into the patient, and force her hand to press against the belly in the form of a cup.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	She finds it, if it is right, that you must move it from great to great in the entrance of the bladder up to the knee; until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is most exposed, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move your fingers above or below the stone, and let them fit the first joint a little; then pour warm liquid into the joint, if you feel the bone so close to the wound as it can come out, and see how many kinds of stones are: which is to know, small and large, hard and soft, long and rounded, and those that have cracks.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you see the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if he does not swell, put vitriol on the wound, and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, as long as the stone comes out, and have strappings that I told you about in the extraction of stones for your help in your work; and if he does not swell, and this is from the artery that was cut, put powder on the wound and linen strips and do not resume again, lest the patient dies, then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is appeased, and the pus has passed, it returns to your work, until the stone breaks.
de hernie carnouse	of a hare's intestine
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Saltwater is nothing but a collection of moisture or pus, which lies under the skin, where it contains egg white; and it's called "syfac", and it's not actually in the yolk, if one thinks that there's another yolk; and this is the leather of the ovary between the white syfac that we have said; and such things do not happen unless they are.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this saltwater is from weakness, and it comes to the ovary, and spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	In such cases if it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or the color is declining to yellow, or without red, or black, or white as snow, and this happens more often; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then there are abscesses inside, like a cow's stomach, and it does not open at all, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the own flesh, then abscesses are found with a part of the toe, and for that reason one thinks it's another cow; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and white as snow, then it feels swollen; therefore when you see, know the color of the moisture, if you examine all the surrounding area, because the form was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to those who come after the intrusive one, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut with iron, it is advisable to make the patient healthy according to one's power and the replenishment of his body; then sit on top of him on something high, and place above him a great quantity of cloths; then sit on his left, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two horns of the knife; then take the stylus of lead, and cut the flesh of the horse by its length from there down to the nail, and make the incision straight as possible in the flesh of the horse just so white, and burn it subtly according to my power; then perforate the white flesh plain with water until a large hole is made, and extract all the water, and then place your fingers, and extend the flesh upwards; and do not touch the heart of the horse, but only the flesh; cut him through equally in pieces, as much so that you should not cut him well, he will return to the blood; and if the fluid falls on your hand, put it back into his own place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then assemble the two horns of the horse's skin to one joint, then cure him as with other wounds, until he is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the corrupted vein infected with another disease, then it is suitable that you tie the strips which are suspended above, in doubt about the worsening of blood; then strike the vein at all the suspension, and extract the vein, and treat as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, knowing that they are two branches; then strike the other part in the same way as you have done the first equally, then wipe out the blood, and put a linen moistened with rose oil in the wound; and put over another linen moistened with wine and oil on top of both veins, and cover with doubled drapes, and tie up above all the bandage according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the two drapes, and sew them of wool fleece according to this resemblance and assemble them with stitching in the neckband of the braies; and one of the shoulders pinning down at the fundament just under the back, and the other on the part of the finger; and the third pinning above both sinews, and so all assembled the restreinture in the knot of the braiser; and once is medicated this branch with cautery for the size of iron, and that you take a subtle cautery knife, and strike at the skin of the veins, and be scalded as we have said, until the white stuff contained in the blood is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the white stuff with nails, and burn it with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct the patient to treat it in all manners that you can, as long as you are examining everything; and keep the fire from touching the eyes; and know that this work is more healing; and be careful of the consequence of bleeding, and beware of the wounds of cutting; and if no thing causes you harm or an abscess or wound or any other thing, cure what causes you harm according to what has been said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	But if the patient is afraid and will not undergo this work because of its horror, perforate as I told you, for it is when you are certain by the meanings we have said that water flows into a vein; so place the patient on the bed elevated with a stool; then penetrate the abscess in the part below, all over the wide surface, and make the perforation deep in the body; and if the wound is large enough, so that all the blood flows out; then put cotton on the wound, tie it, and let it flow until the remaining blood comes out, and then cure until the wound is healed; and if the poultice does not allow the blood to come out of the mouth of the wound, it is wise to insert a needle or the instrument used to treat dropsy, because its form is as described before; and expand the wound a little more, and know that the blood returns, and is assembled after six months or whenever it enters, and when it is assembled as before, and so will pass away the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that when the cut is made in this part, there are often many deaths, because it seems to be worth leaving alone; and I will tell you about the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from the body and also from the joints, and it is a very frequent case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say that the abscesses are spread due to acidity and water that spreads into the joints or by percussion; and its color is according to the color of the body; and it does not feel pain, but is an abscess. Occasionally there are abscesses that are heavy and hard, with a rough color, and sometimes they come from nowhere and form around an artery or swell in the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is caused by no artery, it is known by the shape of an abscess when you press on your two fingers; and it is not fitting to touch there.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is caused by swelling of a vein is known by its shape at the point of touch on your two fingers, and it can be easily identified by making the mark on this appearance, as well as others; and you must cut with the right finger at the wound's edge, then remove the gauze from above, and release the suspended (or inflamed) part from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already inflamed with these marks, then it is fitting to treat the vein and cut at it; and if it is swollen in the space above the marks, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is fitting to remove all that part and cut around it.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the navel is located at the back of the body, then it is recommended that you copy it entirely, and extract the umbilicus, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are completed, apply the wound of flaxen cloth moistened in rose oil and wine, then the cure of other cures until they are healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the joints.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has been enveloped by a swelling similar to the shoulder joint, with softening of the joints, and the patient suffers greatly when it ruptures; and the cure for this disease is very close to what was done before, and we will tell you about the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit upright on the elevated bed, then lift his shoulders up and down as much as possible, towards all the vessels which are near the veins, and stretch out with great effort; then strike at the spine with a broad motion cutting through the ribs, until they are visible, and then scorch from each part, just as we have said in the extraction of arteries located in temples; then insert an arrow or a double thread into the first place where the vein appears, and tie it to the other side of the head directly; then strike straight down, according to the length of the body, and take out the corrupting moistures; then treat the wound as we have said for all others, so that no single vessel is blocked; because through this there comes no harm, and if all vessels come back with it, then it is necessary to tie the vessels on every vessel; in such a way that the arteries do not lose their movement due to the incision of the vessels, dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the cautery with fire
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Now the consequences of this cut are caused by cutting or sectioning, or when they extend on the belly in the area of the intestines; because the intestines fall away from that injury to one of the extremities; and this injury is either through cutting or stretching, or through percussion, jumping, burning, or lifting a painful injury, similar to these things; for the signs when there is an extension of the cut on the syphus, are that it comes on little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal in size up to the point, because the syphus presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when there is sectioning of the cut, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning; and the abscesses appear in different ways under the skin, near the flesh, because it comes from the intestines and escapes through the cut.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it is bound with the intestines, and retained in the wound, causing great pain to suffer the patient, particularly when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments because of fear, why it is necessary to evacuate them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method for cutting is that you command the patient to tie his intestine to a finger inside the wound if it can return; then sew above his neck between your hands, and tighten the joints; then make the wound from top to bottom, and cut all the skin around the joints, long enough so that the skin can be pulled out; then pour into the incision the intestines according to what you have need for to open the wound, so that they can come out; and make sure they are full so that it cannot come back into the flesh; then wipe off the clean part from below the skin of the joints, until the white parts are uncovered from all sides; then pour your index finger into the one that points towards the joint, between the white part which is under the skin of the shoulder, and between the second white part, and between the one behind the shoulder, and between the second white part; and pull to the right hand inside the wound, and tighten the joints as high up as your left hand; and command the minister to stretch the joint upwards, and release that which is behind the binding; and ask if you find any intestine wrapped around or a hard white part, and if you do not find anything, pour it into the belly from below; then take an awl with a large thread made of 10 threads, and pour it in the back part of the skin, next to the joints; next cut the cords that appear on the thread, until there are four threads; then assemble them one above the other like a cross, and tie the skin from under the joints, which we have said is behind the skin of the joints, with a strong binding of 2 parts; then wrap the strings around the intestines, and tighten them in 2 parts, so that none of the servants who suckle on you can enter into you, unless there are no chafes from outside; and put the first binding according to the second one for 2 times of the length, and after that, leave the skin which is under the joint a double bow, like we said before; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the joints, until it does not have any core, and tie the bow as we have told; then put wet wool in oil into the wounds, and put them in, and tie the binding that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes we cauterize the white flesh after we have said so, by doubt of the continued bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens and leaves the bandage in place until it sticks to him; and if it takes too long for the wound to heal, whether from a hot bath, or apply what we have said, so that it heals; then treat the wound with another treatment, until he is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this book I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in this way: as the ram is wrapped around the bone, in this manner that you tie the belts, after the height, lightly above the lower part; then cut into me, and treat the abscess as we have said, until the belts begin to swell; and cure so that he be completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hairs, so that the muffiee and cures the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is stretched and has no appearance in the cut, and the cautery is made more precise in this location, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Sometimes the skin of the joints is softened in some people, because the flesh that is inside is softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin on the soft skin naturally; then sew the two sides together with a bandage, until you see, first sew three layers of the soft skin over three layers or four tightly, then cut between the layers, and the cure like other wounds, until it is healed, and sew the thread.
dou chastrement	One cautery of fire commands the sick man to let his hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	We know how cauterizations are done according to our law, and I would rather not speak of it in this book; for there is only two ways: one way is that the surgeons should be able to answer when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we have often had need of cauterization in some beasts to help us.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterizations are done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we make by attraction, we sit the patient best in warm water, until their wounds are softened and dried up; then we pierce them with our fingers, as soon as they are relaxed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is to be understood that you should mark the best, and press the skin of the elbow with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike on each one as long as you have scoured them; and leave no small space where the flesh will suck, and the subtle sucker which is under the vespers; and this manner of chastrement is milder than that which is done by attraction, for because it attracts, by chance there may be some thing from the nails, for which the best desires luxury; then cure the wound as long as it is clean.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is according to two manners of home: one is that between the two testicles are open like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes in his groin there is no urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way it is also done in women, with a pointed object just like a splinter.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for hunger and thirst is that you copy the marks arranged all together, and the treatment like other wounds; in the second manner, those men from whom the urine leaps out through the skin of the fingers, have no cure.
de la tentigene	of the toothache
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The toothache is a marked spot on the natural part, until it becomes too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a finger, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is fitting that you paint the overflow of the toothache on your hand or finger, and lightly scrape it off; and do not press too hard, lest there be bleeding, then the cure of another remedy until it is healed; and another mark that appears in the mouth, on the gums, and by chance it bursts forth, and it's according to the shape of a cow, and for that they called it the ancient "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is fitting to copy it, as we have said the method, and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic occurs when the nature of woman is not perceived, or when it is lost; and is born by nature, or by accident by illness that comes upon it, or because of chariot accidents, or deep stab wounds, or stab wounds on the face, neck, chest, back, or in any place; and prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes flower blooming; and knowledge of this is by means of observation of the pulse.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling appears near an injury, choose whether it is on the right or left side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is swollen subcutaneously and it comes close to the two fingers, hasten, and so on: put your two fingers together, and have the woman sit on her back, spread out her legs; then stretch the two fingers, as long as the subtle swelling is, and cover with the lint, in oil, and apply it to the finger, and have the woman lie down at home every day, until it will not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and dense, it is advisable that you cut with a spoon-like instrument similar to mint leaves.
