Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is of the flesh and it comes to a single point, cut there and apply; and with tied-up medicines, as one would use honey, dragon's blood, incense, together many times; then bring in a large poultice of onions, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus be long, and bring in a tent of dry linen; then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a charnel house is found near, then you must cover it according to this manner, if not for the enchantments of the abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the charnel house, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not occur by chance, and when old hemorrhoids develop they become tumors; and we have said in the division the similarities of warts, and the signs, and I will say here which ones receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and the tumor when they are swollen in the charnel house, and do not appear by smell, if it is not cured with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then stand the altar with tongs, and cut at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining bleeding, such as aloe and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet into boiling water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she bleeds afterwards, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall and similar things, and then mix with wheat flour, and moisten with honey and easily, and then apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not so, if they make the patient inhale hot vapors on the back and at the breasts; then take linseed, and the poultice in juice of plantain or in juice of agrimonia with wine vinegar, and make it to breathe on the patient.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is at rest, treat the patient with ointment until he is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and seems like a rough head, so it must be covered as I have said; and then treat him until he is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marrow, such as chancre and a porous abscess and herpes and eczema and fistulas and hemorrhoids and another kind of abscess that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I speak of the abscess that comes to the mouth, which is not an abscess as those which grow on a bow; and if you see how the fire cautery works, then look at whether the abscesses are present in its beginning, being full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let him be cooled until the pain is assuaged; and then place the sick person on a bed, and have two petis sieges or he may recline, and support his back and assemble his feet in such a way that they are away from the leg; and his knees should be spread apart, and bind them with good cordage, and put his hands under his girdle, and tie them well; then bring him the ball to the right side, and attach it to the instrument used to treat the mouth of the abscess, because after that comes its form; and it is necessary that when you see attaching this instrument, that you fix the first needle in place to know the depth of the abscess, so that whatever enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instruments are larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloth, so that the instruments do not hurt him; and it is necessary to put a horn on top of the instrument, and tie it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is closed with stitching, then it is advisable to avoid using iron cautery, but treat it in the way we have said when dividing.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The craftman must be the first to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs that you see when you witness a woman going into labor, and having strong desires to push out: therefore hurry on gently with her abdomen, so that the child is quickly born; because when he emerges from her head, she will give birth to the second one too, and her uterus will be cleansed of its superfluities through good purification; and this who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes on his feet, and it comes to the body or joints, and the hands, or where it comes to the stomach, or sovain, and is converted by chance on its neck, and with other bad forms; for it is necessary to the surgeon that they be clever and subtle in these things, and warms himself from error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon his head by natural cause, and the woman in childbirth screams loudly, and the virtues of her body are weak, then do this: seat her on a stool, or women hold her; and roast her flesh in oil or fenugreek until it is cooked, and then pour the bale between her two small vessels, which has the form
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the vein, and stab at one of its tendons until the moistures that are burning in it; and press the woman's abdomen so that the fever descends; if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cauterize the woman with musk and fenugreek oil; then let her take food and vomit condisi, and keep her mouth and nostrils closed for an hour: if this happens now, the fever
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out free, it is to be gently loosened little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on the bed, and lift the feet up high; then break down the bed on earth, and take care of the woman, so that she does not slip off the bed; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife which is placed before, and extract the child gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the outcome of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, so it is to be pushed upwards; and then turn little by little, until they are even; then take hold of the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it cannot jump just as soon as the cubs, so command to take hold, and make it stretch on its hind legs; if it jumps, then God is with us.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, so it takes time to take place, little by little, until it is according to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	So then it happens more easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not happen as we have said, then take musciliauge of alet (alum), and oil of sismant, and gumma melted, and grind all in mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and avoid this ointment, then make her sit in water until down to the ribs; and when she is moistened down, then make her wear a girdle of mirror, and put it on, and let her rest for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her vomit and strangle her mouth and nose, and take gently her belly, because now the child leaps within.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the issue of the child above his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if you put oil on his bottom and bring your hands to his belly, and hang his feet down and sit him there; then take your fingers apart slightly, and then put them back onto his chest, until he is fitted together below; and if the child does not jump, grasp his feet and hold firm, then hold the chest up, then dip your hands; and pour in oil slowly; and command the woman to fasten herself tightly as long as the child is still inside.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the issue of a child who comes out with one hand in front
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must engineer to return the hand: if you cannot return it, then make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed and hold her knees together; then apply the mucus that I have told you about; and if she does not conceive, then make her sit on a stool; then study to bring back the hand again; and pour in oil according to nature, and let it expel, and command the woman to fasten herself tightly as long as the child is inside.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of a child with his neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards the back on the mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I believe that the black bile is drawn out of his hand, then it turns a little and a little, and it becomes lighter; and when it is equalized, so put on the musk-like substance from above and oil, as we have said, then command her to move a little and a little; and when you have done this, place her on the chair, and she will restrain herself.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner for all these things.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all these things, strike the vein on one's anglebone until the moistures are void; and if the fever sets on his face and on his neck, strike at the root, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then pour the child into a vessel, until you have put him in such a state as is fitting, and command the woman to restrain herself from any movement: thus he will be made lighter.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It has been observed that twins are born many times, and sometimes they are born in pairs of three or four; and this is not a strange thing, because it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are an extraordinary thing, and do not live if they are named; I know that they are multiplied and come forth from the womb, as if by some special power, which is linked to the birth; and sometimes they are born just like all of us, in the same natural way that we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born seriously, then the treatment is as we have said, and it involves subtle balances, and quickly and gently what she does; and it happens in such a way that it is worth taking medicine for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No one is born with the marks I, II, III, IV, V, VI, or VII, or more than fifteen, for they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his body's size, and it must be considered that if the physician believes this, because by chance a similar thing occurs; then follow accordingly what is required.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; and the minister apply to the mouth two parts of oil moistened with muscillaige of althe and fenugrec and seed of lin, then rub the hands of the physician with these oils and muscillaiges; then pour them lightly into the mouth of the wound; and this is the form of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to push his head into another opening, or where he needs to be inserted, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it equally by moving from one side and the other, until it comes out, and holds the wound closed with stitches as it is in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it stays part of the way, apply some oil to certain of his two joints, and pour them into that part, and treat the other part; and if it doesn't stay at all, place this instrument higher in him, and do so until he comes out entirely flushed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and he cannot return to the constriction, so you should cover the upper part with a bandage until it is all dry; then cut into the joint of the foot or knee, and do similarly on the other side, and make two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l'enfant est gros et il est estois en l'issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l'aigue; ou tu la ront a l'estruement qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s'elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s'il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is upon his feet, so that he attracts lightly, and the remedies are applied to the mouth of the marjoram is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is swollen in the belly or groin, so that you draw it out with an arrow wrapped around his hand; and make the belly or groin, until the moistures clear up; and if other limbs are swollen, and the joints stick, then give him balm made from marjoram, and rub it just to the mouth of the marjoram; and give one or two ounces, and draw it through; and if the bowels of the marjoram are retracted because of a painful abscess that has come, it is not wise to struggle, but rather to apply soft and moist things; and apply them after plasting in water, and slicing with milky and soothing things.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the fever is on his chest and you can make him even, then follow what we have said about the living child; and if they do not have any power, then lay him on pieces of cloth, and leave nothing of the second skin.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the limbs are straight as we said about the cut arteries that come out of the neck; and if they bleed again, then take him to water, restraining it, and do other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, and then she consulted another one on her, and refused to let the other die.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time the wound came out in the throat, and swelled so much that it burst, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was unable to complete the task as I don't have any further instructions.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a splint on the broken bone, and after some other days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed at this, because the belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and felt for bones, until the woman was in better condition; and the woman took many days to recover thus, and suddenly a little bowing of her leg appeared; and I have not remembered this chapter since because when the masters saw an extraordinary thing, they knew how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Bring back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of pressing, to which one applies the books; and then again at the second joints of the two bones.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	On must be more subtle in applying the corset, and make it of ebony or boxwood; and make the mouth of the tube a foot wide, and the margin of the trees one foot, and a palm and a half long; and for the two joints shall have two pairings of this same wood, which are set firm in both, a half-palm long or slightly more; and these two pairings are closed in the mouth of the corset to open when turning the two corns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in shape, shall be made from ebony or boxwood, following the likeness of the tongs; and it has two joints with pairings, just as you see, a palm long, and two feet wide; when opening the corset to the entire instrument, place the woman on a stool, over her belly, and legs bent, then close the two pairings together in the corset, and hold the head of the instrument between its joints; then open your hand to the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that opens the mouth of the corset, until it does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all crowned and have multiple forms; and when the mirrors are brought out, it is faster to work on them, and higher up there by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not prepare the instrument that you use it, for its need is no excuse.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second tooth is retained in the child, it is advisable to instruct the patient to bring their aline (tooth) forward, and then have them spit out condisi (possibly referring to spitting or ejecting), and hold one's hands to the mouth and nose; and if it falls off while doing so, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it does not fall off, you may try to pierce it or make a wound, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the child, such as calamine, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all of these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put a poultice or wound-dressing on top of the pot, and the other cheek inside the child's mouth, and hold it until the vapors come out from within the mouth; then have them spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If his second tooth has fallen out immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not better, instruct the physician to wet his left hand in oil of sesame or musk root, and then pour it on nature, and when he wants the tooth, and as soon as he has found it, take hold of it gently and extend it slowly so that the marrow does not get caught during extraction; but they must move lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; if it comes out, it will come out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the jaw of the marrow is tightly closed, we have said to release the treatment and perform fumigation with herbs; and if it is none of what we have said, beware that you do not go mad while treating; but it is necessary that whatever is at the jaw of the marrow, tie it to the chest of a woman, then bind it with ointment tetraformulacon; pour some pepsin and put her back, and she will come out; but all things being equal, when she puts it, if there comes a bad smell in the stomach and head, and blackens the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is therefore necessary, then fumigations are suitable for this case: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which you apply the fumigation to the woman, when holding back the flowers and the second nipple if this is so:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a bow, and put the subtle head in nature, and the hairs wide on the fire; and so apply the fumigation on the coals, and the worm until it is consumed, and repeat another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	But children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, unless it has been softened by a subtle knife: if this is so, then take to the bath and pierce that knife in its place, and do not pierce it with a sharp needle, and tie the bandage so that she does not touch it; then put on a moist cloth in wine and oil, then apply ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not heal, put on a bandage of onion, and let the hands rest for days, and leave it exposed when the fever has gone to bed in the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And there is no time for this sudden bleeding from a wound or an abscess, if you should cover that suddenness: if it is cured, as we have said of the onion.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the root.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come out from under the root are nodules, and those that come out from below the root due to moisture or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or multiple; and when this nodulation is old, it causes ulcers, and encroaches on moistness of the skin, white or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas pass; and they are caused by what is ejected or emitted by the patient, and by chance some come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If it has fistulas which occur at the bladder and at half of the penis, and reach as far as the joint of the thigh, and come out through the navel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so they call out that the fistula continues down to the fundament, and does not continue; and this is how you put your finger into the fundament, and insert a fine needle with iron or linen in the fistula where it has no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, then put a fine nettle or horsehair tent into the fistula, as far as you feel the nettle or the hair, and if you do not feel anything, and there is no discharge, nor wind, nor opening, just like we said: see that it does not penetrate; for this will hasten the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent until it reaches the bladder or just before the urethra of urine, so the urine bursts out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it occurs at the joint of the crotch, it comes to the testicles; if there is no tortuosity or knowledge of the location of the pain, then it is a constant bowing and does not benefit from medicine or surgery by application; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except for labor, and the folly of foolish remedies that intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have experienced; so that the patient lies between your hands on their back; and lifts his legs up to his groin, and inclines his groins towards his belly; then pours a poultice of ashes or pitch if it has tortuosity, until you know whether the poultice comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundation, then it is advisable to apply your two fingers there, if you feel this area before something tries to pierce; and if you discover this or sense a swelling or a lump between your thumb and arm, then know that it is swollen; do not work on it anymore unless you cannot cure it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	But we cannot heal everyone, but it happens little; and the aid that is given to them, if it is a cauterization subtle according to the width of the fistula, as has been said; and pour in full at the top of the fistula until it comes from below the foundation; and make this twice or three times, until you know that these swellings must be burned, which resemble like a bird's feather; and then the cure with wet poultices on melted butter, until those swellings disappear, and then the cure with ointment binding flesh and stitching.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus ill, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If so, no other remedy can be better than this; and if he attempts to pierce between the joints, and does not penetrate as deeply as is necessary, and puts a thick covering of charcoal or pitch on both sides of the tendon, and you see the fistula opening behind that covering, which appears red with inflammation; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and bleed before the tenting, and then cauterize afterwards, until it comes to the head of the tent, he will be delivered from the pain, and cured; after putting on those charlatans' remedies that resemble a swan's feather, and none of them remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not wish you to bleed him, and cuts between you and the wound, so that the cauterization with fire or medicine is applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, there are two things to consider: that is to say, the abrasion of these burnt skin parts, and the contraction of blood and the drying out of moisture; then, cure the swollen belly in butter or raw cheese, until they allow it to bow down, and the fat burns within the bowel; then cure the wound of sudden ointments, which are like a hard char, and so are the medicines that dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is safe and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just at the bottom of its deepest foundation, and is located far from the body, put two ounces or so in the foundation, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the pressure and between two things, it is either the membrane or the skin, or it is near being pierced, if there are no fires but only a way of hope through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you pierce just at the bottom, or if you can, you put ointments and cure as first; and do not go too deep, lest you cover the seat that holds the foundation, and come to the egress by chance movement of willingness; then cure it, as we have said; by chance, if it is cured, or if you push away that covering and the wound is pierced from below, or by some other instrument set apart; then remove the unnecessary thing that was in the wound, so much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the abscess in the opposite part of the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at times, fistulas are created in this manner: and when you put a tent in the fistula, and it is in the groove of the skin above, so that one takes hold of it according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I push the string twisted in two, and put the tent all along the string in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is stuck in the margin of the skin below, then pull out the string from that puncture, so that you put your two fingers on the underlying foundation; and take the top with the string, and assemble the two joints together, and hold them one to another, and let them be for a day or two; and restrain it no more than as long as the strings separate those marks, and heal the wound until it is dried and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not heal, then pierce it in all manners that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to cover the wound if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny plantain seed from which the fistula is made is much thicker in one part and thinner in another; and on the other side it is not so, for that's why you should not pierce what you should not pierce, as you see:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two kinds: either they are inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and sometimes they have blood inside the fundament, and some are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and are cut with a knife or a bit of salt, and have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them in the fundament is to command the patient to lie on their side in the chamber, until the fundament is dry, and you will see the filaments; if they are quick to heal, then take nails or hold it with your finger, and cut at its roots; and if the sinew cannot hold them for their moistures, then take them off a horse's girth, or a piece of cotton, or a piece of camelhide; and pull them out by your two hands, then cut them, and powder on top some hot powders that are in the cautery; or you cauterize as it is said in the chapter of cautery, because the cure of other cures until it is healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then bind the patient with a strong binding and sharp for lathering what is in the fundament, if it can come out openly; when the patients are aware, and if the filaments have dried out the fundament, then the cure is light; and you take them off by your finger or with nails, and cut, then cure as we have said, until it is healed, and that they do not fear the incision with a knife of iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting that you join the stitches according to this manner: take one thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread up above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two joints with the thread below the needle, and if it is wide; and strain the thread firmly, then no longer, and extract the needle, and do so to all of them, and leave one for correction of excess blood; then put a moistened cloth over the wound or in oil rose or cerote, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then let it be until they stop bleeding, and when they are cured, apply ointment and other cures, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	How tightly or loosely the thread is tied to the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There are times when severe pain occurs in the intestines, and by the constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset at the point of a splinter or on the nail the scab above, which does not allow moisture; then treat as long as it is healthy if it suits; and if it cannot heal, resume the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals completely and is scabbed over; then treat as long as it is healed.
dou fremit	do not vibrate or shake (the text seems to be incomplete or corrupted)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The formic appearance is a false sign that appears near the body, and goes deep into it; and at times the heat of the formic appearance, and the sensation of being cold, like death, come out from within, and spread all over the body, especially to the hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the patient to take a stick of one goose quill or a strong bird's beak, and place that stick on the flesh, until the red circle appears all over; then turn your hand all around the stick until you cover the whole circle, and put it into its roots, and secure the flesh with its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see, make such a thing of a thorn or iron according to this form, and be subtle under and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't pierce it, for you must hold to the two, and press And if you see, cut off the red circle, as you do in front of or near the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a hollow cystor (or possibly "hollowed out")
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	There is no blood evacuated when using silver or lead, or melted tin or cloth; and sometimes one uses these small instruments and large ones, according to which they are suitable.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then one uses in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small or large syringe, if it is too long, or if the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a rupture or the belly is bound, as you see, and the syringe is filled with what appears to be there; and one has an opening on one side, and in the other, there are openings, and it is felt that they have I holes per side, and the belly is sewn up with medicines from a cow's bladder or parchment, and are visible all around with small openings, each having one hole of space, then put in I thread of rope strong as leather into these I holes, tightly twisted, and assemble the belly like an arrow; and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument at the edge of a cord, then syringe; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And so let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint his head with lard or oil or something similar, then pour it in lightly; then grasp the physician's hands together as if he were dead, till all is well, then pull out the plaster, and lift up the patient's legs to show, and if the medicine comes out as it can, so be it; and if he sleeps a whole night like that, so will there be greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster him when he has a disease of slow-moving belly, and the medicine rushes out, so that it comes back as soon as he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament, or abscess, so that the plaster is applied as finely as to a child; and it's this form of the subtle plaster where the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	For we have already said in the division the cure of wounds; or you will tell us about the cures for hands and medicines, according to what has been completed.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to how they are done, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things are done because wounds are made of piercing with stone, cutting with sword and knife, or lance or stick or net, or similar things; or what is done according to the nature of the body, such as a wound that chokes on the neck, head, shoulder, belly, liver, or other members; and I will tell you about the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds on the head, since memory will come back in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I'll translate the text line by line into English.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if he does not wish to recover, so that his flesh becomes thinner, and he drinks no wine, nor eats meat; and put on the wound, in case an abscess comes out, a wet cloth soaked in olive oil or vinegar solution; and if there is no abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh throughout its depth, and not moved by air, powder, I will say one thing here later; and if he has moved the part, put on some ointments, until he is cured.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be sewn together by stitches, then sew them together by sewing, as I said for wounds in the belly, of the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered of bone and is torn, and does not stay but falls apart at one point, then be cautious; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore the skin to its original state by applying leather, and instruct the patient to eat large quantities of meat, such as fowl and bread, just like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting skin or leather that is rotten to the bone, and it tears completely apart, and falls off, then cure it; and if an artery has formed in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines without cutting, then choose to cut the artery, and if you find it constricted with a thread, then tie it with a string; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light; and it is that you put on this powder which unites as well as the arrow has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to take powder thus: take charcoal one part; dragon’s blood two parts; calcined vinegar three parts, and make the powder subtly, and apply the wound, and tie it tightly, until it has dried well and joined all of its sanc; then bind it well, and let it be tied again, if it swells; for you do not remove medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this done alone with calcined charcoal, when one does not have either the charcoal or dragon's blood, but only has the powder of herbs moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the herbs have moved the wound, especially when it was fresh, do not put this powder on it; but place some digestive ointments or poultices made from flour of barley watered with milk and honey until it gels; then let the patient be treated by other remedies until they are healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, so that I put fine stitches upon it; and I will tell you here after about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	But if the wound comes on the neck and it is simple, unless there is no difference between the neck and the head, but if the sinews of the neck or the arteries are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But if it is the sinews, you must not put anything else in the cure, and do not tie anything to restrain it, because it hurts at night and makes them retract; and putting anything on the wound does nothing, because the substance of the sinews is cold, and the continuation of this is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if you have medicine, so that calomel is washed in sweet water, and melted with olive oil, and the calomel is also washed again in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that the cloth and bandages can bind it, then the treatment continues until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are very deep and he has a head and is full of pus, then cut more lower; and if an artery is cut and blood flows in, treat with cauterization; and if the esophagus is cut or the throat, keep the conduit secure because the meat will move, cut the wound on the chain of the neck, but not touch the neck itself, rather follow its natural shape, and immediately bind him, let him rest for some days, then apply treatments with herbs until he is healed; and if the wound has pressed against the bone, treat it as such; and if there are pieces of bone, cut them off with all haste, and those that cannot be removed, leave them so that the wound may heal, dry out, and become clean again; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow wounds or sword wounds
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is an arrow or sword wound that has pierced and the patient is dying from loss of blood: then it is understood that the wound is mortal. If not, and if the wound is fresh and all its sinews are intact, do not put powder or bind it with bandages on the wound until the first hour; nor should you bind it to the sinew unless I have said so before, but rather look to the heart, and treat the patient accordingly; but apply soothing ointment, and tie it twice a day. If you don't have ointment, put fine cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if no spasm comes, nor does he show signs of severe pain from the heart, or strangulation: and when you see his bones are recovering, it is understood that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Instruct the patient to apply poultices and other remedies as long as he is healthy; and if she cannot heal or recover, then look carefully to see that there is an abscess; if the treatment is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, on the front, back, or sides, when treated for that which is in front; if it is large, sutured; and if small, poulticed; and if pushed into the bone, and there are punctured pieces, whichever suits the wound, and removes the foulness if they exist; and if they do not exist, then allows the wound to dry out, so that the extraction of the pus will ease it, and for other wounds, the judgment is made as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Letting out the contents of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Letting out the contents of the abdomen is great and small; because of the large wound, no intestine can be left, nor the joints of the intestines, for that reason they have to be let out; and the costal area is more painful, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, for this reason we put in fewer stitches on the intestines when we don't put them back up, because they swell quickly and feel pain, so they go back in again, and for that reason it's better to have a clean cut, so that we can put the intestine back in its place like others do; and I will tell you how the operation of letting out the abdomen is done in four ways: two common stitches are used on the belly button, and the stitches for other types of wounds on the body are also common, but there are two other specific stitches that are only used for these types of wounds; and all of them are more suitable for the belly button operation, and I will tell you each one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I have a small wound and there is no blood coming out from the intestines, and it's not very painful to treat, this is one of two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, treat him in one way: moisten the wound with a sponge or one pound of cloth soaked in water only, or cook in water with vinegar and spices, and then stop the intestines until they are deflated; and do this sometimes, so that he may be cooled down and deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or boil it and boiled meat, because by this the entry is blocked by a little thing; and if it cannot enter, do a small wound at the instrument of which they strike the varicose veins; and first do what reduces the size, so that none should cut him until there is great necessity and he needs it; and these are the instruments to split: pierce inside in the horn and avoid not, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines bulge out, then restore it according to its natural shape in its own place, if you have the power, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, if it so happens that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then raise the head and the stomach higher than the lower parts, and similarly consider that when treating large wounds or small ones, you must take this into account.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.
