Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be extracted, leave it alone for a while, and then continue the extraction until it comes out; and if it is still stuck in the arrow, pour the contents of the arrow into its shaft; and if it has been cut, and you see that you must administer an ointment, do so with an instrument of the head, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then pour out, and if the arrow is stuck, pour the instrument in with a point inserted in order to relieve the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is stuck, it is advantageous that you copy all the flesh around or where the venom is, if possible, and then treat the wound as it should.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If they are shot or pierced or in the stomach or bladder or on the side, and it is close to a vein or a nerve, and you cover up if you prick them; and you must avoid covering the vein and the nerve, and then take out, and then bind the wound, if it is necessary; and the treatment until they are healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and thus are:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the hair holder at the end is similar to the feathers of a bird, in order to push onto the tip of the arrow.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of nails to press down on and to apply a poultice is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Veins from which one is cured are XXXI, because there is sixteen, namely: two branches that are after the ears, called "doug herbech"; and two arteries in two temples appearing; and two veins that are in two cheekbones of two eyes, called "aspire"; and the vein at the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars that are around the neck; and the two veins above the lips of the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are cured commonly are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is located on the left side of the body, called by the common people "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it by the common people "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side, called by the common people "vein of the belly", and is above the diaphragm, and that is the one that cures, which opens clearly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the artery is the one between the auricular and anular bones, and in two places; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one of them is under the wing of the little finger on the left side, and the second vein which is called "nasse" is at the ankle on the right side; and there is a third vein that is called "lesse", which is located on the other side of the other ankle.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are after the ears can help with ancient catharses and migraines; and the quality of the sinner is such as I tell you, and it is that you lift up the head of the sick person, and rub the vein or the veins on a rough cloth; then tie the patient's neck to a wooden ring, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places: if they do not work, and you feel the poults under your neck, it is said that enche; then take the lancet, and pierce through below the vein until you see; then drain and tie, until she is cured; and I have already told about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the sickness of the cephalic vein for ancient maladies, and for emigration, and for inflammation; and those qualities are such that the patients turn their necks in twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "foisseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and press upwards of your hand, or with another thing, and let the wound bleed according to how much you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is clean and never again has a sharp edge.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	It is not right that the edges be too sharp; and the healing of something crooked, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the edge when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The patient's head and neck are of little help if the arms are injured, and the chest, and the back, and the side, as well as the disease of the face; and those who suffer from such injuries will strain their neck by twisting any rope, just like before; then they will recover, and so it is said to be the treatment for a wound that goes through the breast, one inch long, one inch wide, because there is no hair.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the splinter is fine, by chance it breaks; then make a cord of the wound, as much as you have need, and then tie it up tightly, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The wound of the vein near the neck is very valuable, and a strong sore, and diseases of the face, such as emigration and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and those who have suffered from wounds like this are said to strain their neck, then strain their neck with your left hand, and take out the fine splinter, and put it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and if you do so now, she will start to recover; and don't go too far, and make a cord of the wound according to your need, then tie her up for one night, because she is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the splinter:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to bind the arm tight, and at the beginning of surgery, and for many illnesses, and emaciation, and corruption, and herpes, and injuries; and the qualities of the disease are such that the patient should remove his neck from both sides, as we have said; and let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient sit in the other side, then cut a vein of long length slightly, then drain the wound temperately, or until it is necessary; then make another incision in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tie around the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and let him go to bed just at night, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	About the disease of the liver.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sick of the veins on the lips, above so are aided with coal in the mouth, and with corruption of gums, and tearing of lips, and no pain or inflammation.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the blood is such that it is to be done by sitting the patient in front of you, and straining his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one being on the right upper lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them: strike then both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, strike the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the wound below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	When the wound of the veins is below the tongue if helps after the head-wound, and it's at constricting the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and if you cut well after such a treatment if the patient dies between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks below each corner one vein black: cure then both sides, and do not go too deep because there are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck are cut in two common ways: either by poking into a large mitten-shaped mark or an olive-shaped subtle point, which is called "anestil"; and they are cut large or subtle according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The fire cautery has a long history and is very well known, and it is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins on the neck with a large scar from a great wound that contains many wounds and pus; and this is the form of the fire olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle in its point, and it is for healing the veins subtly, where there are subtle wounds lemon.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps in healing the diseases that are below the throat, and on the neck, and on the side, and on the abdomen; and it is necessary for the physician to apply a gentle treatment, and to draw out the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he hits the artery, and bleeding comes out, then he must stain it, as I have said; and he should not prick the flame, but cut like an ass.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open up immediately, then it is necessary to extract it, and change another one; or you want any rain in it, or you sew the vein at the root of the arm: it opens up immediately; and cut the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the pulse of the vein, then it is also necessary to extract the arm, so that you touch the vein until you know the pulse; then mark the place with a bandage, and tie the arm, and cut the vein at the flame as we have said; and beware that you do not prick the artery when you see the swollen vein, for this is an artery: thus avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to look out if it is protruding in a way similar to the urine of an infant, and if they are not red and subtle, it means there is no artery: hasten then, and put on the bandage long enough, then take off the bandage when they do not bleed much, as it happens many times; tie up your arm, and leave it like that, and do not move the patient's limb; and be cautious, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	But if they do not bleed when cut, and you see that it is coming out, and the medicine does not bring relief, because the artery is open, and the head of the vein is retreated, stop cutting.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of scar tissue and cut it, and take one half and tie well to the other tomorrow; if they do not bleed, this is good; but if so, as we have said, apply the powders that stop bleeding; and the bleeding will not be worse for mortals with smaller wounds, and the power of the tied wrist.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Instruct the patient to let the blood flow freely while treating wounds on the head and body, since it is composed of basilic and cephalic humors, as we have said; and it is fitting for the lord that he warms himself by the nerve beneath, and if he pricks too hard and causes more pain, he will find the nerve, and it will swell and his injuries will worsen, and by chance, it may not heal; and this nerve often opens many times, and if it does not open in any man for its subtlety, it is fitting that you apply oil to the instrument again; and try to remove the nerve with your own strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then let it run to the long end.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic humor is alleviated by treating wounds on the head and assisting with the eyes; and it is fitting to relieve pain in piercing with olive or myrtle flame, because this is the most safe of all veins, since there is neither nerve nor artery below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Everyone should seek the easier treatment first, and do not grieve over anything if it is needed for the first time, and start again; and by chance the swelling may affect some people when it happens for the first time, but it does not cause anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is not brought on unless for the purpose of preserving health, and to get rid of diseases before they come; and it should be done in one of the three veins: head, elbow, or groin; and it should be done at the beginning of prayer times, especially after Easter and Christmas, when the sign of replenishment appear; and it should be done on either the first day or the third day after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is being treated has no certain diagnosis of his illness, but rather depends on the time of day or night in all hours and at all times; and it is not advisable to heal children before they are 14 years old, nor pregnant women unless for four months prior to their delivery.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	It is not advisable to heal those who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed in any way, so that it may happen, if one takes the intestinal contents of a light castor oil, if he has much retained feces, if the veins do not draw out the intestinal superfluities with harmful members; nor will he heal who is too salty of meat, or who is sick with fever, in any manner whatsoever, until he be cured, whether by sickness, vomiting, and deterioration of the bowels, and frequent urination, and fatigue, watching, and striving, and all this by virtue, either of arms or of body; then subtle the humors, without being too fat, by foods and drinks and medicines, to see if it has worked well. Then enter a warm bath, unless anything is forbidden, in order to subtle the sickness, and cure you from the pain through the third, as we have said; and beware that day of work, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be careful and cheerful, and let the healers be higher than those who are being healed, and tie your arms twice or three times, because when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be drawn out without a mistake; then frot the hands with salves, until they swell, and feel on; then press the sainieres firmly with the flame of a bit of old oil, then put on her a strap of your left hand under that vein when she is being healed, so that the vein does not burst and will fail to be touched by the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that run just like strings to the veinkeeper, and there are those that are full of windiness, so when you put on the flame, it retracts, and can't open the vein, and is thus treated in this way; and if you cover the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore, wise scribes must be advised about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then reapply a little lower or above quickly, if the veins become swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen, and the patient fears, then let them rest one or two days, and don't tie up the arm: perhaps there will be abscesses coming out; nor should they enter the bath, then reapply the treatment when it pleases them; and if the wound is shallow, or if they want to cut through it subtly, then doubt that it will not burst forth as you see, so fear that same hole with the whole flame directly; and open a little quickly, so that the swelling may go away; for this has happened many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swollen limb, do not restart the dressing again, and put some pouce of oil upon it, for it lightens the body from the wound, and is moistened by the oil; and thus administer pouce of oil in each dressing that you apply to the veins, to stop the flow of the wound's blood; and this same thing does good and serves as a remedy when you put pouce of oil on the limb; so subtlety and sparingness are necessary when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a great abscess comes in which has happened many times, especially when the vein is only open at those times or when the opening of the vein is small, you hasten, and put on the limb a moist sponge soaked in water and with a little salt, and restrain it for an hour; it is to your advantage to do this after the issue of the wound from the vein, and if it stays on the limb for several days without any sign or color, it will not be harmful; and if you see, put on some aloes or mirror juice remade in calamine, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: take your hand up, and if you find it swollen at the point of pressure of the hand, then that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put on any of what we have said, for by chance cutting without an artery; but dry the wound first to harden it, then apply another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it be left to issue until it is red; and if you see it is large, let it be left until it becomes subtle; and if it is too hot, let it be cooled.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	Instruct the one who is strong and robust, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the gashes be wider; and for the weak, do the opposite, and it will be more beneficial and frequent, and you must heal him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is safe from bleeding out of veins and numbness of nerves, and is worth more than being healed with a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him who needs bleeding to heal his blood, it is beneficial to give a meaty poultice in the juice of green pomegranate; if he is hot, apply it three times or four; if he has a cold temperament, mix the meaty poultice with powdered pain in honey syrup, or with aromatic honey syrup flavored with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the hand is bound with a bandage, after much blood has been drawn, it is fitting that he hums broth of vinegar and sweet syrup, and uses other things as we have said in this division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to vent out some of that arm, and make it healthy again, it is fitting, when he is weak from great blood loss, that he heals a little at a time, according to the continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to vent out some of that arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong constitution, will heal in seven hours after the first bleeding, or perhaps at nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed of another side, so that he may heal the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is severed, so let it be left and do not tighten it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if a wound needs to be treated the second time, so treat it in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein swells with the arm because it is swollen in place of the vein on the head, for this is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of swathing if it is that the patient pours his hand in hot water, until the swelling subsides; then tie it lightly, so that the vein appears well, and now treat the wound with a strip, not too wide or too long; and if there are large strips, and you sew them well near the joint of the hand, and they do not burst out, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the wound heal in the water, until you have enough; and if it remains like this, do not pour the hand into hot water again, for one puts it more in a state of fever than in a state of calm; and swathing from this vein is safer than any other vein.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the salvation of the right hand is worth all diseases of the belly, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the wound opens, if you see; and if it opens the wrong way, and if you hit it all around, do not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are quite raw from the bone, and then put the hand in hot water again, if it is not frozen in the wound, and will not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut the wound as necessary, put oil and thread on it to sew hastily, and do so for every one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do it just as I told you to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is worth more than all other diseases that are outside the body, such as sickness of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his spleen are such that if the patient drinks hot water and puts a stone in it, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and puts above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and through the foot they go much blood; so it heals then or becomes larger at the ankle, or is made larger.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you save the joint above the foot, so beware of the nails that are below, and the healing through as it would be like cutting; and may the wounds heal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be removed, he must put his foot into water, and let the vein be well cleansed.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the suture is not good the first time, he must reattach it above a little piece because the foot is salt; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and do so with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the ankle and its pain is like that of the calf when it's inflamed.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the quality of its pain is such that the patient is in the bath, and he strains above the ankle for four days, because otherwise the vein does not open; and when it opens, tie him with all the means you can, and cross him over; and make sure that you copy what has been written, because the skin is tight, and they are very much swollen at home.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it true, then the man will have pain in his head or in his back on one foot, and towards the small toe, and beware of the swelling; and make as much care with the wound that you see, and then release the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; he is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wind sickness
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wind sickness is made of horns, or thorns, or glass; and wind sickness is done in two manners: either by wounding and drawing out the wound, or by wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this wind sickness which is done by wounding and cutting out the wound is done in twelve places of the body: for some are all in the head; and others in the neck; and two others in each side of the neck; and the wind-sickness under the chin; and under the shoulders; and under the eyebrows; and on both arms; and on both legs; and on both ankles; and it does not treat wounds, except for small cuts scattered throughout the flesh, as is done with a vein bleed, because it weakens no one, just like when one bleeds from a vein; and it should be avoided, neither hot nor cold, in any disease that comes from overeating, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it's swelling in the morning, we order that he be ventilated after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The inflammation of the tonsils relieves the distress of the head… when it comes to the eyes, and should not be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the inflammation of the cephalic region, and should not be used by those who have cold complexion or constipation, because it causes great harm; and therefore, do not use it on those who have watchful vigilance, or those with head colds or fever.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and therefore should put the ventilation device a little lower by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wound on the neck is in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it must be constricted at the waist, and cut open of the channel of the pomegranate, and swollen, and replenished; and one must not push too much, because if she holds too tightly, so it will lead to an obstruction or a twisting of the stomach or the liver.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wound on the neck is in place of both the breasts of the neck if it causes pain to the head, eyelids and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is near the vein of the basilica; therefore one must command the lord that he presses his hand so that he does not cut the artery, and does not come in contact with the blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wound under the chin is in place of diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is near the veins of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders value a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the sides are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because they bring forth blood from these large veins; and instruct the lord that he should not pierce too deeply, for the nerves and arteries are bare there.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the backside is worth as bruises of the fundament, and of diseases there; it is necessary that the wound be great and of earth, to well treat it; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and thus it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds on the legs heal widely because they draw forth blood from all the body, and are worth ancient pains of the rain, and of gout, and of bladder, and reduce swellings; and are equal to two groins, and two knees; and they weaken the body after a long time, and make come fever in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Instruct the patient to put on a ventouse first when it is empty and well-tempered, and hold it in place firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease this until you see the vein turn red and swollen, and bleed from the wound; then stop, and remove the ventouses, and be careful with the body, because there are many who have such a serious case, and you can use clerestory (holes) to gaze at them: it is necessary to cut once only, and it is wise to make large wounds, and deep ones as well; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is small, so cut again twice: once to subtlety the way of the large wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is wise to cut a third time; and when we want to treat the small wound little by little, we should strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	Instruct us if you wish to draw much blood, so often we will repeat it; and if the wound is deep, take two fingers inside, and press hard until the edges are perceived suddenly, and cover that which has thick skin and firm flesh, for they have more pores, apply oil of apricot, or sweet almond oil, or oil from the seeds of cucumber, and if it's in yver, then use oil of cresson, or of lye, or camomille, or any similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the ecchymosis is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or aneth oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If that person has healthy skin and large pores, do not put oil on them, but rather wash with water from a rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, so lifts himself up from this place, or from water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And he who has large superfluences rises up from old wine, or from water of sycamore, or from aniseed decoction, or from camomile, and similar things; and does not take medicine beforehand with vinegar before the bath nor after the bath for one hour or two; and does not sleep afterwards when he has been bled and when he is bleeding.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And therefore if one who is cured has colic, and his belly is not too swollen and inflamed; then it is suitable for him to take cold things, such as apples, grapes, endives, and lettuce at rest, and similar things; and pure broths, and charcuterie of chestnuts, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Et cil qui a froide complexion, so he should drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and little meat, and eat small and small fowl and birds and pie; and the day it gets loose, he must drink more than eat; and it's fitting to give some people vinegar or mustard once a year before loosing wind, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let subtlety be without, but it's not fitting that those who are stout should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The ventouses that are placed to inflame are those placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and on the gout, and on the belly and the groin, because this member does not suffer from being struck at, and is only forced when there is an attraction of blood from one part to another, just as we put ventouses on the breasts when they are sore; to loosen the viscosity that is in the limb, just as we put ventouses on the belly and on the groin to soften the limb; and to relieve pain, when there is inflammation or piercing, relieving it by its attractive power by chance, or stopping the piercing of its place; and thus done when placing a ventouse on the liver and on the mouse when there is retained swelling, and these ventouses are empty to suck only; and sometimes they are placed with fire, and sometimes plain water, just as in certain diseases that cause pleurisy, and in such a manner that we fill the ventouse with hot or cold water, or with herbs cooked according to it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cautery administered to the patient is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And they should have two fingers of length and half a palm from the root, and one finger inside the middle with a small puncture, as if to put an awl, and it is made of iron, soft towards it so that it does not prick the patient when placing on the limb; and in the middle there should be a cross-bar of iron or steel, to hold a bandage in place, and they are large and small, according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones are more suitable for weak people than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this ventouse on the limb: take a bandage of wax or linen and place it inside the ventouse through the cross-bar that is inside the ventouse, so that the light may be at the bottom of the ventouse without burning the patient; then put it on the limb, and let the two fingers we mentioned above, placed on top of the puncture, so that when you want to release it, if there's vapor, you take out the ventouse; and take a bandage as before, and rebind often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of someone with inflammation of the pleura, who is sick with fever, has no pulse or pericardium, and is brought in only when they are full of fever, and placed on a limb alone, that's how it looks:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction is only applied to limbs where you cannot put suction on the smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; and in their nostrils, like two or nails, and other similar ones; because of the quality of the user, if you find that they are in soft, clear water without any injury, take them; and place a nut in clean, soft water, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their bellies; and then be suceded by vein and suction, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the suction; and when they are full, and clear, if that's possible to put suction, do so because this is much after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, then lift the limb out of its bed, and then to water, very well, and then inspect; and if the limbs are too healthy after the treatment with poultices, wet the dressings of linen in cold water, and put on them, until they are dried off; and if they dry too much, put vitriol crushed or salt, or similar things, until they are dried; or you put on moist peeling of fava beans onto the limb, and let them be there until they are absorbed by the limb; so it will now heal; and if you have more need, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not take effect, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or prick it with an awl until the poultice comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the wound, they will dry; and when you see that they are dripping, then powder some aloes and crushed silver, or cinder, so they will now dry.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and its treatment involves restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know well, dear son, that the art of this chapter has never been found in any of the ancient books or letters, and no one can read them; and because of this, the science is lost in our land, for I have not found anything good among them; and I know nothing except by the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied thoroughly and treated, through experience, and by my daily custom; and I have written down here what contains it, condensed at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are needed, just as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in this prologue of this book the matters of the word and the chapters which the wise men put their understanding on, and to keep silent, so that those who have experienced it will learn and acquire this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break or dislocation or twisting or cutting comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, so that no one thing hinders you, due to weakness of body, or illness, or old age; or if the joints are too loose, or too cold; and do not give them hot foods, such as chilled soups, and charred meat of fowl and deer, and do not drink wine, and do not eat any fatty meats, and do not stuff yourself too much with viands that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is an open abscess or spread of material on the limb; if the patient returns to their previous behavior.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bones start to restore themselves, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that produce great swelling, or where there has been viscosity, such as when bread is cooked in water, and broth, and milk, and eggs, and pork fat, and fish, and fresh beef, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For nourishment produces swelling, which represents the breaking (of bones).
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that old and decrepit bones cannot be well repaired or soldered again according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure, for you will place a large splint over the broken bone, which holds together the joint with the member, so that it becomes as before; and do not make them work too much, because for this they must be nourished with great foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And so it has been discovered that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that split open, and others that cut in, like the thickness of a goose feather to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And when there is a fracture with an open wound, and also fractures that have just a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own instrument and proper tool for restoration, according to what the memory tells in its place; and it is known that fractures of bone occur because of the joint's twist, and are wide open by nature, and sound like a crack when pressed on with the finger; and if there isn't any twisting or crookiness where the joint touches, and the patient doesn't feel great pain, unless there is no fracture; but it can still have some twisting, or splitting, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not fitting to move your hand, but apply the medicine that comes after this, and then bind it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the broken limb that is in the arm, and are two parts joined together, you must now put them to equal point, so that abscesses do not come; and if abscesses come, you should leave it alone for a day or two, until they are healed; then place it at ease as you can, easily and surely; and know that the restoration of this limb is lighter than the restorations where there are pieces; then bind it, as needed.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and you extend two parts, whether it is a great limb or a small limb, or two cords, or one cord and a small limb; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb are cut short, you should rebuild on all kinds of joints with the help of your art, as much as possible, and take care that through your work, there does not come to the patient any further lesion or pain; and repair well both joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient will feel it well in the hand if you think that it is not right: if the dressing is set up perfectly, and not too tightly strained or pressed, like those who make them come by their work, incising and contraction to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is put to rest, instruct the patient well that it does not move at all, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and take good care that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	But when it feels no pain at all, it is not entirely at rest, and you must put him in a suitable disposition so that he feels no pain; and take care that he is placed correctly, lest twisted movements occur when he is restored to his former state; and the quality of the broken limb will be according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The member is broken in different pieces and in various sizes and forms.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For the small members, like arm and shoulder: cover them with soft, moist cloth; and for the larger ones, like thigh and knee: cover them with a wide and strong bandage. The broad bands encircle the entire limb, constricting it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap. Then tie around the top of the break with light straps, three or four according to the size of the member, and bind your hand tightly on the strap, then go up to the top of the break and tighten less, until the break loosens a bit; and smooth out the bandage gradually, so that you grasp a large portion of the healthy limb; then take another bandage, and turn back towards the broken part; then go down to the lower part of the break and tighten moderately, not too tightly or too loosely, as we have said earlier; then put cloth or rags between the bands until they are evenly spaced; then tie everything up from above with a strong band, and then put your well-made straps on top, if there is an abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, put up a soothing poultice to the abscess, and who cuts out the inflammation, and leaves it for some days; then strain on those arteries, and make a caustic gash of one-eighth inch in circumference, or of wood used to make flails, or palm fronds, and do according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is fitting that the artery which one puts on the break is slightly larger and wider than the others; and be as long as it needs for the limb either small or large; then strain on those arteries just as you did at the first ligature, then tie above with a thread so quickly as in the first ligature; looser is above, tighter below; and it is fitting that the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, but of good flax cloth, for if the thread are thick, as I have wanted to make works from foolish folk who made their ligatures from twine of linen yarn twisted, and this is a great error, because the ligature cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and does not suit that there should be between each artery less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the arrows of these stars after being restrained in their healthy state, he places over them sores of linen or wool, so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is with a fracture and the bones are broken, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not wise to strain the bones of all the members the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the members are large, it is not wise to put a bow on them every day, except after 4 or 7 days, or more, according to the security of the surrounding area; and see here how the ancient surgeons used to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour from which is held by the walls of the mill, mix with a great quantity of lard, and make this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of restoring fractures in many ways, especially women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
