Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering restores the break and dislocation and twisting: take barium and ladanum and myrrh and asafetida and gum arabic and mugwort; 30 parts of mira and aloes; alechil VIIII parts; and make a powder, and mix with honey and vinegar; if their complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is good for twisting: take mugwort and vismalve, 30 parts; mira and aloes, 70 parts; acacia 6 parts; Armenian boric 30 parts, grind well, mix with water or honey, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting involves joining and binding bones with their joints, and after the injury, applying soothing remedies, and using the bone to make the wound: take a new linen, mix with milk in ease and oil cooked, and place on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plaster wraps do not heal, but they are good for soothing swollen abscesses and properly cleaning the wounds.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of splinting that heals broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and earthy leaves, crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of splinting for restoring the break of the bone and to alleviate the swelling of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of vimalve, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, from each one a part; and crush, and mix with wine, and warm the limbs by this mixture, or mix it with moist coriander water, or cold water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying plaster more forceful than the first, when an abscess dura at the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of vimalve, and the seed of flax, balaustre, melilot, sansuce, and flowers of violet and camomile, from each one a part; and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras writes in his book that one should not put on a broken limb for restoration except the cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it must be between too hard and too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that we must put a linen cloth over the broken limb, to restore, things dry and warm, like mirrors, aloes, and incense, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat a wound and pain is: take horse meat or crushed bones, or goose feathers, or vialle ( likely "violet" but also means  ' violet colored powder used in medicine'), and crush them equally, and put it into the wound, and let it be.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then let the swelling go down after a while, and take care that if the patient does not feel any pain, nor does he lose his bone in its place; if not, do not let it be handled by hands for three days. But if pain comes to the limb, or it prurites, with rest or inflammation, haste, and remove it, and now put in a dressing, and take an sponge soaked in moist sea water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased. Then let the member rest for one hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened with water or olive oil rose, and tie it around a nut, until you are sure that no infection has set in; and keep the inflammation away from the member, and let the pain be removed, then resume subtle handling, and not strain the limb too much as before; and handle subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has turned into pus and is red and painful and swollen, I have taken out all of it, and you must fill in and bind again, since it will return, as you did when you first made it even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb that we have spoken of, do not release or untie it after three days or four or five; and never let it stay for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break is healed, and approaches the joining of the bone above. Then restrain it more tightly than before, and fatten up the flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb is drying out more than necessary, know that no other remedies can come to it; so now take away the swelling from the member, and hasten to do what the foolish doctors do, which causes the member to be twisted: this is bad, and there are many painful remedies, and I see nothing else but loosening and over-tightening it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of breakage
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks, and various forms, and the causes are determined; for there are breaks that are made by striking with a spear, and the collarbone is fractured through the shoulder joint which lies beneath the bone, just as it happens from a blow or a fustigation; and hence this kind of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the spear strikes through the bone from above to pierce it, and this kind of break is called "absolute"; and there are two kinds of injuries resulting from these two types of breaks: great ones and small ones.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has a puncture or a wound, or a fracture of the collarbone, or cutting into a stone, or hitting on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is persistent fracture, which approaches just to the skin on the bone below, or above the bone, and this wound is big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered by a thin layer of skin just like our own flesh, and there is a small crack, and for this reason, such a fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a piece of stone or falling, or by some similar thing, and the bone fragment enters into the space of the bone, and the bones are so swollen as they would be when the blacksmith heats up the black iron on the anvil; it goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones such as the head of an infant, and it occurs in all these kinds of fractures so that small fragments are separated like stones.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by pulling apart their parts, and investigation has been done, and by the corruption on top of them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs it upwards, if it opens up the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be careful about accidents in patients, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, emission of speech, extension, pausing, fever, eyelids swelling and redness, and other similar dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any extraordinary accidents, and you expect salvation, as soon as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when it comes to you first for treatment, and it is in winter, so it is fitting to pull out the bone before the fourteenth day at night, that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, so hasten to pull out the bone before the seventh day, otherwise the wound below the bone will be corrupted, and accidents that we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone break comes just next to the covering of the brain, so it is fitting that you split the broken part in this way: and take the head of the patient who is dying, and uncover above the bone in all possible ways, and according to the shape of the wound as best you can, and if bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone, or the abscess is exposed, so you should assist with it according to what is needed, and it is that you fill the hollow place with moist cloth soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calm, and be sure of no further bleeding; then begin to extract the bone, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut at the tight cutting beforehand, and it is like this form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then after this cut, a more thorough cutting is done than before.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have to do several cuts of different sizes, some of three and others of more length, with pointed edges and made of iron, and doing them lightly so as not to strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, it is wise that you pierce through it, so that with cuts you administer with tapers, not by piercing too deeply, lest the point go beyond the bone of the skull, and on top of the point, there should be a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have more, so that each comes in its place according to the measure of the bone, so that you have tapers for all test; and this is the form of the three kinds of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Injuries that pierce through the bone are such that you place a stick in there on top of the bone, and turn it back to your two hands until you know whether the bone is pierced; then put the stick another time after a little while apart, and do so all around, then cut at the incisions the space between the pertus, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take out the bone from your hand, or from any of the instruments you have, such as tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you pierce the bone and take it out, if some remaining part is left on the bone at all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it should be more subtle and more precise than the others; and if no small bones or scales are found, if the bone can be easily removed from any of the instruments; then cure the wound by applying tenses and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of work is that which Gallien says, who is more skillful; and he speaks very loudly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where or at which the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place below the head of this incision lens-shaped, because this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut into one part, and the parts are affected in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then using a small hammer above, you should copy lightly the bone all around, and be well guarded of the cloth that is under; if it is rough against the bone, cut lightly, for cutting the bone easily, because one cuts badly with pain, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone is broken and pierced only just beneath the skin, and the bone is struck so that it has small pieces, then cover again with that roughness, and remove the scales from the subtle rasp which you must have in various quantities, to fit each person as comfortably as possible, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have before many rough rasps, and after finer ones, and do not stop doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, it is fitting to fit according to its direction; and this is something that has not been replied by anyone who put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sutures are exposed, it is fitting to tie a linen strip according to the quantity of the wound, and apply rose oil in it, and place it over the wound; then take another strip doubled into two or three, and anoint it with wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first strip; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you don't bind too tightly the suture, but rather let it heal slowly until the swelling is gone; then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vinegar, and incense powder, and other similar things; and make a powder from these things, and apply it to the wound, and administer the medicines so that they may be absorbed through mastication; and beware that the wound is completely closed, lest you leave on it the suture or assemble a bow, for when a bow is assembled over the skin of the brain, it gets corrupted and causes great harm to the patient, because when something sharp is placed on top of the suture, it causes necrosis from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Precautions then, if no other accidents come to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a black spot does not come up except by the medicine we have placed on it, which has virtue, then it is fitting that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue I wrapped, and apply it to the wound; then perform the cure with cures as needed, until he becomes sane.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Which of these have been broken into two pieces, or the one alone, for these are two bones; and that which is below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then becomes sound.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you pour your small oil or resin into the break, and put it inside your thumb index, and in the pouch so that the bone comes back to its natural figure; and do this gently, so that the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If they break in the upper part of the neck and cannot come to life again, so you should place an equal amount at the head of one inch a large rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is of two parts, you should do the same thing, and hasten to restore life on the first day if you can; but if not, after the seventh or fifteenth day, when the abscesses are calmed down, then boil with wool wrapped around the neck in order to cover up the break which is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you pour the other into that place, if there is a break; and let the tents be as thick as they fill up the gaps of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said that the restorer said we must moisten the tents in butter, and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem right to me, but it is likely that they are moist in the making of both of honey and flour, then let the tent stretched out until the bones harden, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time put on ointment of onions in its place, and if it has a swollen lump around, and keeps the wound still, then blow into the patient's mouth and see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the neck while you are working on it, put a crust or cotton soaked in rose oil or in a poultice of dung.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, put plaster on due to before, made of flour of sesame and powder of incense, mixed with honey, then put light strips on it and do not bind the wound; and if the bruise in the neck is small and broken into little pieces, if you take suitable instruments for this, then cut the incision and the treatment for wounds that are hard to clean, and sewing, if he has no wound inside the abscess, then apply plaster and put cainches of plumb, until he be cured.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the tooth extraction of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is cut below, and there is no wound hidden, only a slight fracture without splintering or breaking into multiple pieces, if one notices lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is advisable, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your left index finger inside the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side of the jaw, put your right index finger into the same place, gently push the fracture inside and apply pressure with the other hand, even though there be hidden.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is twisted to the right side, it is advisable that you stretch out two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth happen, or fracture, so the strain on one thread of gold or silver or silk, then put the broken jaw on the surface and coat it with fat; and put up a double layer; and put up one well-made needle or piece of leather long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above the muscle that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so the dislocation is done three days, and then put it back to what was changing; and apply plaster on top, with powder from ground wheat or sesame, after you have applied the fat; and put on a linen cloth light, and if the plaster sets, and the patient’s disposition does not change, let him remain for as long as he heals; many times he heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes from a wound, so to speak, then do what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, then reward yourself with no piece of bone left after it has been removed; so subtlety in removing the bone is considered acceptable.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then expand it as much as necessary according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces of bone, and it does not stay in place at all, then count the wound, if it is wide, and apply some suitable dressing to it, to heal it so that it becomes sound.
de la forcele	of the swellings.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force is broken multiple times on the shoulder, and there are three ways it can be broken: or it is broken and separated in two parts, with fragments, and it is lighter to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the wounds are in such cases when the break is with an open wound, that you have two ministers: one who applies the balm to where the force is broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break on your own, so that the form is as it should be, and there be no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, put an iron ring over the shoulder of the sick person, round and made of cloth or linen, so large as needed; then stretch the wound and bind the ring with your hand, so that the break is set in its proper form.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If the fire cautery cannot be applied to the forehead because it comes out in full, it is advisable that the patient should lie on his back with his hat over his shoulders, and have a warm drink poured into his shoulder until the bones of the forehead are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the fracture to your two hands; if you find broken bones, it is advisable that you cut them; and carefully remove the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot be joined together because of any swelling, cut into one of the incisions you have made; but place the forehead with this instrument, to ward off the syphilitic.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not made of wood, and should be as large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and have two ends, just as you see, and one should be wide and the other narrow, just as is the routine of the wound that you have made when you broke the bones; and when you are certain of a swelling, cut the wound, and if the routine is small, or you doubt the swelling, then use the wounded area with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes upon it, so that it moistens the dressing in oil of roses and in ash and in wine, and puts it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is sensitive to wounds and swelling, is that you place the bone over the ointment of powder from the mill and of buckwheat and wheat flour, and put light plasters on top, and if necessary, put a spear below the joint; then take a great bandage of one palm's width, and put double plasters on top of the plaster, and the ointment; then take a fine needle of three dobs in length and six in width, and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the needle above the fracture, and turn the bandage up towards the neck, and below the joint, so that the joint is still, and not painful; and pull each part tight, and when you see that the limb holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the limb is conformed, and you release the binding; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow below the joint, to lift the assistant up high; so as to alleviate the swelling of the fracture by the tightening of the shoulder, or by tying the arm to the neck, and not releasing if it happens again, for twenty years.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is broken or displaced, keep it in its place by touch; if the limb appears according to the shape of the break, and straightens itself according to its natural form, in all possible ways that you can. Then put on the limb powder from the mill with a great amount of wine and fine pieces, and tie tight over the limb with a double cloth; then place upon it a large and subtle stake, one piece larger than the shoulder, and carefully remove it from any point of the shoulder, so that you may apply powdered stitches of linen on the stake, so that the stake cuts evenly; and then bind it tightly to its proper place, so that the stake does not move from its place, and examine each joint every day; and whenever he complains, tie tight again, and put an equal amount of bandage over the limb, for the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number has been completed, release it, and be sure, for it will not be legless from being bound too tightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone has burst forth and pointed downwards outside its skin, and below it is not clean, then push upwards and make the bone, and do as we have said for relieving an abscess in a painful place.
de la brisure dou pis	of the broken foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The flesh is never broken in its middle, but it happens often, and it breaks frequently outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downwards and causes great pain to the patient, and lacks warmth, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the vein on the broken bone, and the feeling in the limb becomes worse.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And restoration is to have the patient lie on his back, and put a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two ribs with his hands, and subtly place equal pressure in all ways that he can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plaster and strips over the subtle part of salt, or of another light material, and tie them tightly around the broken bone, so they do not move; and turn the knot round to the back, and tighten immediately, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it loosens, re-tighten it; and if he wishes to untie, because of corruption or itching that comes to him, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie, and scrape the plaster, and address those who came from this by means of cures; then remove the plaster, and bind tightly until he is healed.
de la brisure des costes	From the breaking of the sides
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	He knows that the breaking of sides comes only from their large back after the spine, and their chest, and bends due to them being swollen; and he feels it very badly at the examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you set the break equal if possible.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster and bind with a stake if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of sides inclines towards the belly, he feels the patient very great pain and puncturing, like pleurisy, because the bone pokes the membrane; and there is nausea, and vomiting, with great bleeding, and that's from a serious illness, and the old ones have put in great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	If there are those who say it is suitable to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to calm the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless an abscess forms in the flesh, if it has come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, to cure it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that no one should put vacuum tubes on the limb, to suck out the humors, and it seems right, but there is doubt that the vacuum tube does not attract the superficial humors of the limb because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that no one should cover the limb with a moist linen in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to straighten the curvature of the limb, then either be cured with the cure of pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if he feels great pain because of a bone that presses on his intestines, and doubt is with him, then it is fitting to break up the bruised area of the broken rib, and it is fitting to put something under the instrument to protect the wound; and thus one must pierce the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound if they are large, and cure the patient with plaster, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes forth, then put on moist cloths in rose oil, and put under the patient; cure while the abscess is drawn to the level where it must be incised, and if pus accumulates above the chest or where it needs to be drained, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no break in the bone at the neck of the shoulder, and little happens when it bends; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to you and you see whether it will be healed or not, if you prepare yourself so that if you see your hands become soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that these conditions are mortal and occur in many ways; if they are silent and feel well when you strain them and pick at them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient is cured, if medicine is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing occurs at the spine of the back, and you know whether it will heal or not, prepare yourself if the fingers are softened, and if they are affected by accidents, when they fall towards your hands, and your back bends with violent movement and excretion without voluntary effort; and when someone is aware of its presence on his abdomen, it falls with involuntary excretion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	He knows that death is near: if he does not labor in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident did not happen to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the healer should reward him if he has an abscess cold, if he puts on hot oil or oil of myrrh or butter of beeves, until it is pacified; then puts on a warm compress and ties it with a bandage, and commands the patient to rest; and does not lie down on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are severed, it is to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are great, with a suture, then treat the wound with bandaging wrapped in cloth, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the knees", take out your left hand pouch and put it equal to the other hand's power, then put the compress and splint on, if you have need; then bind him, and if he has a severed bone, cut off, then remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of a bone break of the haunch
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the haunch is broken, and if it has, if not because of a little softening at the head; then let them cut long and decline to the pardentens, and it will come to the patient pain in the same place, point, and swelling where the break was.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, until you are above the break; and see which way the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head alone, then tie up that break, so long as it has its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then lie the patient on his belly, so that the restoration of that break becomes clear.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have made it even, then put on the plaster, then put on a stake of wood or iron, and restrain the break, so that it does not move; and apply the plaster under the ribs, until they are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes up, do not touch it, until the abscess is eased, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to restoration, and restrain as needed, without any additional harm; this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder break.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which lies between the shoulder and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two manners: where one manner is to take a straight stick of bone, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Instruct the patient to bind both shoulders with two bands, and place them high, then tie the bandage around both arms until they are swollen; then put a poultice on the broken arm in the shoulder, so it may be eased, and put a covering of wood under the joint; then put a bandage around any weighty thing, which the servants will stretch out; then put the splint back into place with your hands assembled together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to turn the patient on their back, and tie their hand to their neck; then command two servants to tie the one who holds above the break to his hands, and the other below all the bindings, and stretch each one out to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tighten both the lower and upper bindings around the break, and have each of the servants stretch out to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	In case of a shoulder fracture near the head of the shoulder, so that you place one straight thread below the humerus, and another towards the bone, below the break; and if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is so advisable to put one lighter thread gently, with effort, until the break is equal on both the joint and the bone; then set the break, as needed, and bind it, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess comes, and it is not bound for seven days, put a moist cloth on it in ease and in rose oil, until the abscess is eased; then bind it, and the way of binding it is that you place plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or under the breastbone; put a bandage, and bind onto the shoulder joint, and onto the arm, so that the arm is in its own place, unless some thing prevents it, or if the bones are loose.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bones do not move, then use esthetics, and place a larger and stronger stake on top of the break, and have two stakes between each stake, with one stake so large that it passes over the break three times from each part; then strain above the stakes, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on breaks.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the position of the stakes and the straining, as we have said, in the wound where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess, if it does not form within seven days, as we have said; then look at each one of three days the bond, which prurites or swells, neither comes to life, nor brings on inflammation to the member because it is too tightly strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such accidents do not happen, then let him remain still for three days or more, and the patient lies on his back with his hands on his stomach; and he places the shoulder above on one big cushion of equal wool, and looks at each hour of the day whether the figure of the broken member does not move, or is loosened by the ties; so if it adheres by virtue of medicine, and he gives him food that we have previously placed before him in a similar manner, so that the meat be finely ground; and when it comes to take it again, then it is stiff.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reunited after forty days of being in this position; and therefore one must disjoin them and administer a bath and medicine for the joint to set properly.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the constriction is tied up tightly and blocked, he should wait for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the two "fossicles", one small and one large, because the small one contains the pouch; and the other large one is under, towards the small bone; sometimes only the large fossil breaks, or sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fossils are broken, the restoration is light and easy, and healing occurs; but when the large ones break, it is a bad healing, and more grievous than when both together were broken.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fossil that has been broken alone, then you should gently extend it and put it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If the great swelling is, then they must draw it out more strongly; and stretch upwards in the cussin, and pull up the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the petis lower than the others, so that the patient crosses over himself, and the cussin before him higher, that the patient may not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's hands to the part below his hand, or to the joint, and one other minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no shortage of bone that can fit the joint, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make up for it and put in the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If he has broken his limb, I have already spoken to the singular doctor about it; so take the care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, there appear swellings on the skin, then if a dressing of rose oil made with olive and white wax is applied to it, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind up the dressing gently, until the swelling subsides.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the rose oil, and put on an ointment of powder from the mill with a lot of vinegar, until you cover it with the splints, and make the splints as strong as possible, and just a little more wide than the others; and see that there should be six splints or more, in one disposition: whether the break is in one bone or two; and tighten more above the break than elsewhere, and every day less when you remove it, as I have said at the beginning of the doctor; and make sure the dressings are soft and moist on top of the break, and not too hard or sharp; and use the thread from which they have strained, either linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accidents happen to the limb, so that it pricks, as when it pricks happens to the limb, then it is advisable to raise the limb in hot water until the prickling stops, and let the limb not be too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the bandage, and if the bonds are loose and the bones are laid bare, and a similar thing happens.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you cannot apply the poultice to the limb because it is too tightly bound, then it is advisable that you loosen it a little, and let it be for some days, until the inflammation subsides, and then reapply the bandage.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient, who does not suffer from it, for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	How long the fingers are bent on his neck, and so that his neck is even, and he guards against movement and numbness, and lies on his back; and you know that this break is restored in thirty days or in forty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the humors and the complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that behind the hand, there are often two fractures, and only pain occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And if the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, it is necessary that the patient should cross his arms and sit up straight always; then he places his hand on an extended back, and extends his broken fingers, and puts them in alignment as best they can; and he applies plaster and casts, so that abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the injury; and it is wrapped up in one fold of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In case of a fracture in the padded area within the belly of the foot, make a spear of drapery and instruct the patient to tie it around his broken foot; and then tighten an arched rope, so that the weight is as great as the weight of the foot of the hand, and tighten it, just like it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is in the finger, it is advisable to put an arch on top and another below the foot; so that the fingers are straight and upright, then tie them all around the hand, and anchor the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture comes to either of us on the thumb, if it is swollen, make it even, just like it needs to be; and tighten with the foot, and if you see that putting an arching rope small to lift the fracture doesn't move; and if the fracture is in another finger, whether in the index or one of others, put it even, and tie it to the healthy joint next to it; or tie all of them together at once, as much as you can, or put on an arching rope, just like the swelling; and be careful with restoration and disposition of the abscess site, and heal those who come to you, just like I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the cross breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the cross is often broken, and if it is seen that the joint turns both in front and behind; and the restoration is as one binds above the break, and also below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient swells on his face, then each of these ministers extends his bandage to his equal part; and this is when the break is mended with the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the cross, so that either one of the ligatures towards the finger, and the others towards the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the groin, and then so that either there are ligatures towards the groin, and others above; then put on the splints the bone equal to its two hands, as much as its nature dictates, and then apply the plaster, and the ligature, lest there come infection.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, then let him calm it first, and then return to his work and his treatment; the relief is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap up the limb in a bandage for two or three days, and keep the swelling, then turn the leg so that the toes reach to the root of the nail, and pour one long cloth between the thigh and leg, from below, and tie it tightly above; then twist above the leg and above the thigh the bandage, then put on the broken limb stitches, and put a stitch on the bone of the leg; then wrap soft cloth around between the leg and the thigh to tighten equally the ligature, then start to tie in figure three or four times above the break; and as you go up further with the break, and less the straining; then hold two threads of the cloth that you poured between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stitches that are on top, then return below to the head of the cloth, until you see the bone; and the straining, if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, then when no new abscess or swelling or other appearance comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	In case there is one, if the joint is dislocated and addressed as described, so that it is just like we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that grip, then it is advisable to keep them, if possible; and if not, then it is advisable to split the limb, and cut away; and treat as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is broken like that when we put in stitches, just as we do in the shoulder and arm; it won't come loose, so by that restoration nothing will happen to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And knows that the skin is restored in a few days, or perhaps less than that, or perhaps more, according to the various differences of complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the gouty vein
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	When there is a fracture of the neck, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it's only a tear or separation, and it causes all wounds and pain, and the wound is deep.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put equal that which is torn onto its two ends, until it's assembled again, then apply plaster, and put a round iron nail if necessary, and bind it as needed, then follow all the dispositions we have said about other fractures, just like the abscess and similar things; apply to each accident what is fitting for him, until he's healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	They say that in the thigh there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all other fractures occur when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done as equally as the arm, and the wound is entirely one. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bones are broken, feel great pain and see it well; and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then apply an extension, and put it equal, and tie the bands equally; but note, if the break is uneven, and there are more pieces, that the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have completed your work, so take two faxes of gauze that stain the leg from one side and the other, and are long enough from the knee down to the joints; then wrap them both around the limb, and the bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is well; and no one should give too much gauze to the length of the leg, and if it's stiff, and it's wrapped, and one puts on the leg to ward off movement, and it is properly done in the break where it has been injured; and move each limb every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fracture of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not come from any break, but sometimes the bone is broken and has to be put back in its place, and there are no other injuries except for swelling.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.
