If it has a bone break and you see the bones overlapping one another, put the malaide's foot on the ground so they do not move, as if they were going to run, and then put your foot on their own, so that the bones are raised, then press them tightly until they come back into place; then apply plaster and poultices on, and put a small wooden splint on both sides of the foot with two pins, then tie it firmly around, and other things as you require.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, you will find the joint loose again, because you will discover that the bones are in place, whether they are broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Instruct the patient to let his hairs grow long and even; and if he pricks at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, since we have spoken of them; and cure each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break in the bone at the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, if she lays it (flat) and enlarges, then incline her to the back part of the back, and hold her there behind; then fill the wound with cotton as thick as my finger; then tie down the woman, lift up her back little by little, and then sew the cotton, until it comes into the opening of nature, and returns the bone with (the same) thickness; and when she wants to urinate, if she has pulled out the cotton, then put it back in, and thus do this for seven days or more: if she is restored to health, and you see, take a vessel of wool, and tie a rope around the broken joint, and pour all the vessel into nature; then blow into the rope until the vessel is emptied inside: nature will return the break; then fill with cotton, and let it be so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the thumb, in a man or woman, is broken, restore it as we have said about the os of the hainche; and these nearby fractures are not concealed from one who puts his study and his use there, and takes heed of this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these breaks signify an increase in more dire dispositions on the right path of restoration; therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take an owl's gizzard and apply it to the wound; then wrap strips around, and let him be wrapped up for three days or more, and he will soon be healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it's large, such that the bones of the scapula or shoulder or similar areas become healed now, so that the remedies we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is sound, then set back the splinter of glass, if you have nothing else, then restart to heal the break in the same hour, or on the next day, unless an abscess comes upon the flesh.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes upon the flesh, then let the restoration on the next day, until the splinter is appeased, and do not touch it or come near for a week, lest you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and appears near the knee uncovered, it is fitting that you put it at a light point with your fingers, to an extent that is small.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not fitted to be put equal with your hands, and the instrument that is made of iron, which has seven or eight fingers long, and the width depends on the quantity of the wound; then it is the work of the surgeon to take three or four, according as he needs in each cure of a break, and so it should be strong and one middle finger large, not deforming under compression on the limb at your request, and so the middle finger ahead, and big from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the cuboid bones should be placed above the visible bone of the head; and once a blow, until it returns to its normal state, so that the one corresponds to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the splints cannot well take hold of the bone, so that it is advisable to copy the head of the bone, until the splints have a chance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot set the bone as we have said, so that it is advisable to copy the head of the bone with a suitable instrument, such as a knife or saw, at your ability; then take back what remains in the bone from harshness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is known that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then make a hole in the girdle of wine vinegar black, and properly clean it; and do not put anything else on the wound except for oil, lest it come to rot and corruption; then administer remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the break; and many times they have done this like fools, and have brought the patient either death or corruption once; and so the gentleness of the other breaks are softer and more gentle.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is serious or large and you doubt that more accidents will come upon it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so it is not wise to apply remedies; but instead cover it with a bandage, stiff, in place of remedies, ties.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound has healed at the bowels, then check what you have put above on wine, and apply salve to healing wounds, as ointment quadrupharmacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is fitting that you should remove the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is fitting that the limbs be applied in such a way that the bowels run down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the wound transgresses and it cannot heal but by re-opening of the bowels, see that you know where there are small fragments of bone, because it is fitting that you should treat the wound with cautery, and remove all these small pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the leg, or another kind of corruption, so it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he said in his chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and opens up on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones in the great members, do not treat it immediately, because many die, but leave it until it purifies; by chance it will heal after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can, and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on from the supuration.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and what an ugly thing to see: the figure of the limb; and by chance, it cannot do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	One limb which is weak after childbirth.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and stays after the weak limb and subtle movements, so happens for many causes: because one was too tightly bound and did not stay as it should have; or because there are too many ligatures, and cannot come the nourishing power to the member; or for excessive rising; or for great movements, neither in its hour nor otherwise; or because it has little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until it is multiplied in him; and administer a bath, and give joy and ease; then put powder on the member, so that the powder attracts great nourishing to the member, and the blood rises often from the watery flesh, until the nourishing reaches the member; and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One limb twisted after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	If the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken, and the form of the limb is ugly, it is not advisable to rely on natural healing; do not believe false ones who say that one must break the limb again, for many fools have done this in our land, and these operations are blamed, and lead to great harm, and sometimes death. Unless the nodulations and tortures are fresh, then it is wise to apply an astringent moistened with hot water, or boiled herbs such as violets, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and let it be applied moistened with vinegar well done, and take the muscivage of violets, and confine it with lard or olive oil of sistrum, and apply again; or take greasy figs, and crush them with flour of millet, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is opened by constant and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted one is hardened and hardened, like stone, and needs to be cauterized with iron, so that it may cover just onto the bone at the subtle incision lightly; and add cushioning and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to any of them, so that it must now be reset carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toda voie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters of dislocation of the shoulder joint to be done in a specific order.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated in two ways: either they are slightly detached from their places and softened a bit; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chin, causing the patient to have difficulty keeping their mouth closed, and their tongue can't be kept still with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When small dislocations occur, they return to their normal position through multiple procedures.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and fulfilled, it is recommended to reset them immediately, and not delay it; and in such a manner that the ministers show you how to apply pressure to the patient's head, and pour some medicine from one of their hands into the root of the dislocated mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is by II parts; and the other two fingers are reserved, for equalizing; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And then pour equal amounts until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns with inflammation, especially if both mandibles are dislocated together, pour on hot water and oil until they return easily; do not delay returning to normal, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed tightly with molasses made from oil rose and wax, then tie it lightly with soft threads; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his joints be between two cushions, so that he does not move at all in left or right hand, nor does he struggle to break the bone, but receives gentle food until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are numb; and then take what he wants lightly, and do not trouble himself to open the mouth to drink and swallow, until the mandible is well numbed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be fixed in their place within an hour, and are not converted to their own position, then fever and vomiting come on, and occasionally diarrhea, and sometimes even vomiting blood.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it's a sign of death; and many have died from it in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fist
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fist cannot be loosened from the chest within it and the finger, and is dislocated every time in spite of all effort, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient stiffens on their back, and extends their arms; and then presses the wrist against his palm, and it returns; then puts on plaster and bandage, and binds it; and the head which was opposite to the shoulder cannot be loosened; unless not, and if it becomes dislocated again, then he is reset to its place, as we have said; then puts on plaster and bandage, and binds it, and commands the patient to rest until they are healed; and so is restored the shoulder joint when it is reduced to its proper place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder can be dislocated: one way is that it dislocates at the base of the humerus below; and the second is at the elbow joint; and by chance it sometimes dislocates above, which happens rarely, and does not dislocate either behind the shoulder or inside the arm; but often it slips down towards the bone of the shoulder, just as frequently in those who have little strength, because they quickly become weakened; in those who have some strength, it slips loose at the joints, and returns to the joints.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some people that they hit or crush the shoulder with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary to examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they slide down towards the shoulder joint, and you will find a difference between the sick and healthy shoulders, and you will find various differences manifest among them; and you will find a depression in the shoulder head, and below the shoulder, the head of the shoulder, just like one another thing; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its normal position, nor can they move from any movement; and also, if it is displaced upwards, it is not hidden, because you will find it manifestly at the shoulder; and this kind of dislocation is not too difficult to treat, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The doctor should lift the hand of the sick man upwards, then put your fingers below the elbow, and lift the joint at force upwards to the level; and the doctor lifts the hand, and stretches it upwards because he is putting it down; if it comes together quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come together as we have said for many days afterwards, it is fitting that the sick man be bathed in hot water; and he should be treated with an immediate soothing and softening, like a decoction of althaea, fenugreek, and meliloton in hot water, and so he should be treated. Then put him on his back, and place a linen bandage under the elbow joint, neither too loose nor too tight, then place the fingers of your other hand on top of the elbow, lift the shoulder joint with virtue, and treat the patient's hand; and another minister applies pressure to the patient's head so it does not move; the shoulder returns perfectly now, and if you see that he recovers according to this manner: and thus you should make him be present before a larger person who is standing straight towards his side, and pour water into the armpit of the sick man, lift the elbow joint up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister treats the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then weigh him with anything heavy, and the dislocation will now return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And in another way also: and it is as follows: and take a long iron bar and bury it in the ground, so that the joint can be straight like the piston, and not too large nor too small; then put on top of the patient, but only if he has soft skin above, and his joints are straight with the length of the stick; then stretch out his hand towards another part, forming a joint, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take an iron bar from two arms long and four fingers wide, which has the head on top to fit into the hollow below the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie under the head with a cloth wrapped around it so that the wound does not bleed into the face, then place the bandage on the face of the patient; and extend both arms over the body of the fistula, and tie the strap around the body, and the arm at the head of the hand, then lift the arm above the elbow, and let the hands down, and leave the body hanging from another part: now is the time to reset.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in whatever manner, you should put below the fistula a spear of wool equal, then put on the bandage a poultice made of powdered flour with incense and myrrh on all the shoulder and around, then strain from beneath the fistula immediately, and turn the tie onto the poultice, and wrap the hand around its neck, and so let the hands stay thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is fitting that he moves little, until the members are comforted, for he will be cured faster; and then move more after five days or seven, and he will be healed; and if he is firm and not softened, he is already healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture that has occurred, or for another reason, it is fitting that you administer cautery three times, as he is placed in front of the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days he becomes dislocated again, and the joint will not stay in place, and cannot lift even one arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder have been pierced or stretched or softened; and know that the joint has never returned to its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs at the wrist and elbow, or behind, is done by impulse and stretching of hands, and it serves another joint; treatment until he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes grief to the limb, and slow movement, apply the patient many times to hot water, until that grief is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Which joints of the shoulder are displaced at certain times, and again return; and if they are displaced from all parts, and even in front and behind, and the dislocations are not repaired, because it is seen clearly and felt clearly; and each displacement corresponds to a shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, so that you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset him thus, so that abscesses come out when they do, because if abscesses come out then, it will be pain to reset; and by chance it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; for this one is worse than others, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is restored, when they can be reset, then, when you extend your hand to both hands; let his arms be spread out, and his hands laid out according to the cut in front, above, and below, and push the joint into its socket or to the root of his palm, until he regains his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is dislocation of the shoulder, so it returns when he doubles his hand to its own hand, and with fear from the root of the palm where it is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, so apply strong extension; and let two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm of each part, when you have wrapped a double length and width bandage around it; and when the joint meets the joint in the arm, apply oil to any point for softening the joint, then make the joint firm, until it returns; and when it is in place again, apply plaster hard with a small amount of wine, and tighten the strain, and bend the arm on the neck of the patient, and let it remain for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, so loosen the ligament and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it be for some days, until it becomes firmly set; then loosen.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels great pain after the joint is moved, and it holds, then bathe him well and rub him gently, and press until he becomes soothed; or put on the joint a sheep's fat mutton wad, then let it be for one day and one night, then pull it, and put the wound in the bath; and when it sweats, then rub the joint temperately, then put back the wad, and then enter him into the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see, put on a warm moist poultice with fat and bind it around; for it will return to its original place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder

des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, it is fitting to extend them with work, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if dislocations occur in no particular location of the back or foot, so it is appropriate to seat the patient either on a flat table or on an upright table, and place your foot on what appears from these jointures, then press with your foot firmly, until it comes round; and when it is even and there is nothing, place under the sole of the foot a flat table with two keys, then form the lock again, for three days, then release it; and make him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocations, and you try to restore them, many patients die: do not be presumptuous in the treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have long experience of it, and unless you are pitiful, merciful, and delayed, do not be hard. Use soothing remedies at the beginning of things, especially antiseptics hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, unless you see no hope for recovery; and when you see hope, fix the limb now as soon as the abscess comes to life; and when the limb is fixed, administer soothing remedies again, and treat the wound as it seems fitting, with dry bandages; and if there is a dislocation with fracture, and small bones broken, set the bones, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into the path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will be yours, unless your Creator has mercy on you, and gives you wisdom, and armor for your body.
Amen	Amen
